<th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-size:125%;font-weight:bold">Nuremberg–Erfurt high-speed railway</th>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center"><a href="/wiki/File:Karte-Neubaustrecke-Ebensfeld-Erfurt.png" class="image"><img alt="Karte-Neubaustrecke-Ebensfeld-Erfurt.png" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Karte-Neubaustrecke-Ebensfeld-Erfurt.png/150px-Karte-Neubaustrecke-Ebensfeld-Erfurt.png" width="150" height="464" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Karte-Neubaustrecke-Ebensfeld-Erfurt.png/225px-Karte-Neubaustrecke-Ebensfeld-Erfurt.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Karte-Neubaustrecke-Ebensfeld-Erfurt.png/300px-Karte-Neubaustrecke-Ebensfeld-Erfurt.png 2x" data-file-width="599" data-file-height="1854" /></a></td>
</tr>

<th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;background-color: #efefef;">Overview</th>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Native name</th>
<td><span class="nickname" lang="de" xml:lang="de">Schnellfahrstrecke Nürnberg–Erfurt</span></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Locale</th>
<td><a href="/wiki/Thuringia" title="Thuringia">Thuringia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bavaria" title="Bavaria">Bavaria</a>, Germany</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Termini</th>
<td><a href="/wiki/Erfurt_Hauptbahnhof" title="Erfurt Hauptbahnhof">Erfurt Hbf</a><br />
<a href="/wiki/Ebensfeld" title="Ebensfeld">Ebensfeld</a></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;background-color: #efefef;">Technical</th>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Line length</th>
<td>107&#160;km (66&#160;mi)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Number of tracks</th>
<td>2</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Track_gauge" title="Track gauge">Track gauge</a></th>
<td><span class="nowrap">1,435&#160;mm</span> (<span class="nowrap">4&#160;ft&#160;<span class="frac">8<span class="visualhide">&#160;</span><sup>1</sup>⁄<sub>2</sub></span>&#160;in</span>) <span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Standard_gauge" title="Standard gauge">standard gauge</a></span></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Minimum_railway_curve_radius" title="Minimum railway curve radius">Minimum radius</a></th>
<td>3,700&#160;m (12,139&#160;ft)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Railway_electrification_system" title="Railway electrification system">Electrification</a></th>
<td><a href="/wiki/15_kV_AC_railway_electrification" title="15 kV AC railway electrification">15 kV/16.7 Hz</a> AC overhead catenary</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Operating speed</th>
<td>300&#160;km/h (186.4&#160;mph) (maximum)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Grade_(slope)" title="Grade (slope)">Maximum incline</a></th>
<td>1.25%</td>
</tr>

<td style="width:auto;padding:0 0 0 3px;"></td>
</tr>
</table>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td style="line-height:normal;text-align:right;padding:6px 5px 5px;">Source: German railway atlas<sup id="cite_ref-Eisenbahnatlas_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eisenbahnatlas-1">[1]</a></sup></td>
</tr>
</table>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p><b>The Nuremberg–Erfurt high-speed railway</b> is a 190&#160;km-long <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">German</a> high-speed railway under construction, between <a href="/wiki/Nuremberg" title="Nuremberg">Nuremberg</a> and <a href="/wiki/Erfurt" title="Erfurt">Erfurt</a>. The line is listed in the Germany's federal transport plan as <i>Verkehrsprojekt Deutsche Einheit Nr.</i> ("German Unity transport project no") <i>8.1</i> and is a section of the high-speed route between <a href="/wiki/Berlin" title="Berlin">Berlin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Munich" title="Munich">Munich</a> and a section of the line connecting <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Scandinavia" title="Scandinavia">Scandinavia</a> in the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Trans-European_Rail_network" title="Trans-European Rail network">Trans-European Rail network</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> It consists of an upgraded line between Nuremberg and <a href="/wiki/Ebensfeld" title="Ebensfeld">Ebensfeld</a> and a new line between Ebensfeld and Erfurt. The journey time between Erfurt and Nuremberg will be reduced to approximately one hour and 20 minutes after completion.</p>
<p>The planning began in 1991 and construction started in April 1996.<sup id="cite_ref-np-coburg-2007-10-02_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-np-coburg-2007-10-02-3">[3]</a></sup> Three years later construction was stopped by the new <a href="/wiki/Social_Democratic_Party_of_Germany" title="Social Democratic Party of Germany">SPD</a>-<a href="/wiki/Alliance_%2790/The_Greens" class="mw-redirect" title="Alliance '90/The Greens">Green</a> coalition government formed after the <a href="/wiki/German_federal_election,_1998" title="German federal election, 1998">1998 election</a><sup id="cite_ref-sz-1999-07-08_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sz-1999-07-08-4">[4]</a></sup> and only recommenced in 2002. The commissioning of the section of new line is expected at the timetable change on 8&#160;December 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-ek-2008-11-40_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ek-2008-11-40-5">[5]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-fw-2008-09-16_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fw-2008-09-16-6">[6]</a></sup> The timing of the final commissioning of the upgraded section is still uncertain.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nuremberg%E2%80%93Erfurt_high-speed_railway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>A trunk line between Berlin and Munich was contained in the German railway network proposed by <a href="/wiki/Friedrich_List" title="Friedrich List">Friedrich List</a> in 1833. The line between <a href="/wiki/Erlangen" title="Erlangen">Erlangen</a> and Ebensfeld was part of the extension built in the 1840s as part of the <a href="/wiki/Ludwig_South-North_Railway" title="Ludwig South-North Railway">Ludwig South-North Railway</a> (<i>Ludwig-Süd-Nord-Bahn</i>). The current route, which was opened in 1851, was not based on comprehensive transport planning, but was a consequence of a network that evolved from 1840 out of lines built to serve local purposes. Since then line improvements and technical upgrades have taken place. After <a href="/wiki/German_reunification" title="German reunification">German reunification</a>, the lines were restored, renovated and electrified.<sup id="cite_ref-etr-2007-494_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-etr-2007-494-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<p>According to <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Bundesbahn" title="Deutsche Bundesbahn">Deutsche Bundesbahn</a> (DB), it would be necessary to construct a new railway line because traffic forecasts showed a strong increase in passenger and freight traffic between Berlin, Leipzig, Erfurt, Nuremberg and Munich. These traffic volumes could not be handled with the existing infrastructure. The quality of operation of the existing lines would be unsatisfactory, partly due to heavy use and long service times, and it would be virtually impossible to upgrade them. Line improvements would usually have significant environmental impacts and would have strong impacts on existing buildings, due partly to dense settlement in the narrow valleys that the line passes through. The requirements of a modern railway in terms of traveling times and speeds could not be achieved by upgrading existing routes.<sup id="cite_ref-etr-2007-494_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-etr-2007-494-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<p>In mid-March 1991, Deutsche Bundesbahn announced a surprise direction from the Federal Ministry of Transportation to develop a new line between Bamberg and Erfurt.<sup id="cite_ref-nn-1991-03-15_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nn-1991-03-15-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<p>Traffic forecasts from the early 1990s predicted a traffic load in the north-south direction for 2010 that could not be met on the existing lines. The operating concept for this target year envisaged 108&#160;trains on the new line each day and in each direction, 24 passenger trains and 84 freight trains. For this purpose an <a href="/wiki/Interregio" class="mw-redirect" title="Interregio">Interregio</a> service (Karlsruhe–Stuttgart–Nuremberg–Erfurt–Leipzig) would run at two-hour intervals<sup id="cite_ref-bmv-1993-71_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bmv-1993-71-10">[10]</a></sup> and an <a href="/wiki/Intercity_(Deutsche_Bahn)" title="Intercity (Deutsche Bahn)">Intercity</a>/<a href="/wiki/Intercity-Express" title="Intercity-Express">ICE</a> service (Munich–Erfurt–Berlin) would run hourly<sup id="cite_ref-bmv-1993-71_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bmv-1993-71-10">[10]</a></sup> over the new line; the old line (<a href="/wiki/Gro%C3%9Fheringen%E2%80%93Saalfeld_railway" title="Großheringen–Saalfeld railway">Großheringen–Saalfeld railway</a> and <a href="/wiki/Franconian_Forest_Railway" title="Franconian Forest Railway">Franconian Forest Railway</a>) would be operated as an Interregio service. The Interregio trains of the new line would run via Coburg and <a href="/wiki/Ilmenau" title="Ilmenau">Ilmenau</a> and the IC/ICE services would run between Bamberg and Erfurt (although some services would stop during the day in Coburg).<sup id="cite_ref-pbde-1995-01_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pbde-1995-01-11">[11]</a></sup> The IR journey would take 25&#160;minutes from Ilmenau to Bamberg and about 20 minutes to Erfurt.<sup id="cite_ref-pbde-1996_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pbde-1996-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<p>The direct distance between Nuremberg and Erfurt is around 175 kilometres, while the travel time in 2009 was around two and a quarter hours.<sup id="cite_ref-brueckenbau-2009-99_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-brueckenbau-2009-99-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Decision_to_establish_a_high-speed_line">Decision to establish a high-speed line</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nuremberg%E2%80%93Erfurt_high-speed_railway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Decision to establish a high-speed line">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Today's new and upgraded line is the result of a decision of the <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_of_Germany" title="Cabinet of Germany">Federal Government</a> in April 1991 to fund the "German Unity Transport Projects", which were incorporated in the Federal Transport Infrastructure Plan (<i>Bundesverkehrswegeplan</i>) 1992.<sup id="cite_ref-etr-2007-494_8-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-etr-2007-494-8">[8]</a></sup> The new and upgraded line was described as a "new project" with a planned total costs of <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Mark" title="Deutsche Mark">Deutsche Mark</a> (DM) 4.175&#160;billion in the area of the former Deutsche Bundesbahn and DM 3.020&#160;billion in the area of the former <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Reichsbahn_(East_Germany)" title="Deutsche Reichsbahn (East Germany)">Deutsche Reichsbahn</a> (1 January 1991 prices).<sup id="cite_ref-bvwp-1992_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bvwp-1992-14">[14]</a></sup> The first Thuringian Minister-President, <a href="/wiki/Josef_Duchac" title="Josef Duchac">Josef Duchac</a>, joined the Federal Minister of Transport, <a href="/wiki/G%C3%BCnther_Krause" title="Günther Krause">Günther Krause</a> for the selection of the route corridor through Erfurt.<sup id="cite_ref-sz-1994-01-26_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sz-1994-01-26-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<p>The construction of the route was recorded in the Federal Railway Development Act (<i>Bundesschienenwegeausbaugesetz</i>). The Act of 15 November 1993 entered into force on 25 November 1993.<sup id="cite_ref-pbde-1995-01_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pbde-1995-01-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<p>The line became part of one of the newly created Trans-European corridors (Berlin–Verona) at the 1994 EU summit in Essen.<sup id="cite_ref-pbde-1995-01_11-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pbde-1995-01-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Planning">Planning</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nuremberg%E2%80%93Erfurt_high-speed_railway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Planning">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In the preliminary planning for the new line between Ebensfeld and Erfurt, a total of seven different options were examined. Three different options were introduced into the route selection process for the Coburg and southern Thuringia areas.<sup id="cite_ref-bmv-1993-71_10-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bmv-1993-71-10">[10]</a></sup> In February 1992, Deutsche Bundesbahn presented three options: one running from the existing section north of Lichtenfels, via <a href="/wiki/R%C3%B6dental" title="Rödental">Rödental</a> and <a href="/wiki/Stadtilm" title="Stadtilm">Stadtilm</a> to Erfurt. The second option would have branched off north of <a href="/wiki/Bad_Staffelstein" title="Bad Staffelstein">Staffelstein</a>, parallel to the planned Autobahn through Coburg and would have taken a route via <a href="/wiki/Gro%C3%9Fbreitenbach" title="Großbreitenbach">Großbreitenbach</a> and Stadtilm to Erfurt. The third option would have branched from a junction north of Ebensfeld and run via Coburg, <a href="/wiki/Eisfeld" title="Eisfeld">Eisfeld</a>, Großbreitenbach and <a href="/wiki/Arnstadt" title="Arnstadt">Arnstadt</a> to connect with the existing Eisenach–Erfurt line at Möbisburg.<sup id="cite_ref-sz-1992-02-08_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sz-1992-02-08-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<p>Critics of the project proposed an eastern route, via <a href="/wiki/Bayreuth" title="Bayreuth">Bayreuth</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hof,_Bavaria" title="Hof, Bavaria">Hof</a> through eastern Thuringia and western Saxony, with a connection from Leipzig and <a href="/wiki/Dresden" title="Dresden">Dresden</a>. This option and an option that would have run near the existing lines with an approximately 42&#160;kilometre-long tunnel through the <a href="/wiki/Franconian_Forest" title="Franconian Forest">Franconian Forest</a> were examined and discarded.<sup id="cite_ref-ek-1993-4-34_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ek-1993-4-34-17">[17]</a></sup> Others suggested an eight-kilometer tunnel through the top of the crest.<sup id="cite_ref-sz-1993-05-15_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sz-1993-05-15-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<p>Deutsche Bahn also considered a 24&#160;kilometre-long base tunnel for the crossing of the Thuringian Forest. This alternative was rejected on the grounds of high groundwater pressures (near aquifers), the need to pass below the target storage level of the <a href="/wiki/Goldisthal_Pumped_Storage_Station" title="Goldisthal Pumped Storage Station">Goldisthal Pumped Storage Station</a> (together with additional sealing of the tunnel) and the need for much more elaborate safety measures.<sup id="cite_ref-koennings-1999_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-koennings-1999-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Preliminary_planning">Preliminary planning</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nuremberg%E2%80%93Erfurt_high-speed_railway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Preliminary planning">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Deutsche Reichsbahn initiated the pre-planning in the summer of 1991. A preparatory study had been submitted to the central administration of the Reichsbahn (<i>Zentralen Hauptverwaltung der Reichsbahn</i>, ZHvDR) in November 1991. It served as the basis for the preliminary drafting plan, which was prepared by the <i>Planungsgesellschaft Bahnbau Deutsche Einheit</i> ("Planning Corporation for German Unity Railway Construction") from early 1992 and confirmed by the ZHvDR at the end of 1992. At the same time, a national and environmental protection planning study was carried out with the participating federal states and the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Agency_for_Nature_Conservation" title="Federal Agency for Nature Conservation">Federal Agency for Nature Conservation</a>. Within the scope of a space sensitivity test, a large-scale corridor investigation was carried out on the scale of 1:100,000 to determine route options. Among other things, conflicts and risks in relation to spatial and environmental factors along with railway operations and economic aspects were taken into account.<sup id="cite_ref-etr-2007-494_8-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-etr-2007-494-8">[8]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-pbde-1995-01_11-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pbde-1995-01-11">[11]</a></sup> According to the planning as of mid-1991, commissioning would be carried out by 2000 if possible.<sup id="cite_ref-db-1991-4-13_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-db-1991-4-13-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<p>The preliminary draft plan of 1992 envisaged speeds of 250&#160;km/h with a journey time between Nuremberg and Erfurt of 75&#160;minutes. The planned costs were DM 8 billion (about €4 billion). Already in 1993, before the beginning of construction, the route handled 80&#160;passenger trains during the day and 200&#160;freight trains at night. In 1992, five options were developed that would have passed through a 20&#160;kilometre-wide corridor, one of which was immediately rejected. A route through Coburg that would have required the demolition of existing buildings was also considered. At first the use of the existing line south of Coburg with a new line commencing on its southern approach had been considered as the favoured option. The Thuringian Forest would have been crossed at its narrowest point, but there would have been no stop in Coburg. In a citizens’ initiative, Coburg citizens collected 13,000 signatures against the route.<sup id="cite_ref-spiegel-1992-20-75_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-spiegel-1992-20-75-21">[21]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Spatial_planning_and_route_selection">Spatial planning and route selection</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nuremberg%E2%80%93Erfurt_high-speed_railway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Spatial planning and route selection">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Landesplanerische-Beurteilung-VDE8.1_Bayern.pdf" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Landesplanerische-Beurteilung-VDE8.1_Bayern.pdf/page1-220px-Landesplanerische-Beurteilung-VDE8.1_Bayern.pdf.jpg" width="220" height="311" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Landesplanerische-Beurteilung-VDE8.1_Bayern.pdf/page1-330px-Landesplanerische-Beurteilung-VDE8.1_Bayern.pdf.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Landesplanerische-Beurteilung-VDE8.1_Bayern.pdf/page1-440px-Landesplanerische-Beurteilung-VDE8.1_Bayern.pdf.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1240" data-file-height="1752" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Landesplanerische-Beurteilung-VDE8.1_Bayern.pdf" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Bavarian land planning assessment of 30 July 1993 (full text)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On 5 October 1992, the Board of Governors of the Bundesbahn and the Reichsbahn determined the route of the new line.<sup id="cite_ref-ek-1993-4-34_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ek-1993-4-34-17">[17]</a></sup> The spatial planning procedure was launched on 20&#160;October 1992. The Free State of Bavaria gave its opinion on the 1&#160;March 1993.<sup id="cite_ref-pbde-1995-01_11-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pbde-1995-01-11">[11]</a></sup> It confirmed the compatibility of two options with the goals of land planning.<sup id="cite_ref-bmv-1995-8_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bmv-1995-8-22">[22]</a></sup> The essential requirements were an ICE stop in Coburg, the replacement of embankments by bridges in ecologically sensitive areas, the relocation of the planned over-taking station in Dorfles-Esbach to the south and the lowest possible crossing of the Main valley to the north of Ebensfeld.<sup id="cite_ref-pbde-1995-01_11-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pbde-1995-01-11">[11]</a></sup> An option, which involved a route through Coburg, was abandoned in this context.<sup id="cite_ref-etr-2007-494_8-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-etr-2007-494-8">[8]</a></sup> In its opinion of 20 April 1993, the State of Thuringia sought, among others, an <a href="/wiki/Interregio" class="mw-redirect" title="Interregio">Interregio</a> stop in the Ilmenau area, a shift of the line in the <a href="/wiki/Gehren" title="Gehren">Gehren</a> / Gräfinau-Angstedt area to the west, a western bypass of Molsdorf to protect the drinking water catchment area of Erfurt and the bundling of the route with the A&#160;71 autobahn between Erfurt and Ilmenau. The planning approval procedure (as of mid-1994) would be carried out jointly in accordance with the railway law for both routes in this section.<sup id="cite_ref-pbde-1995-01_11-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pbde-1995-01-11">[11]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-baukultur-1994-3-25_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-baukultur-1994-3-25-23">[23]</a></sup></p>
<p>Between Ebensfeld and Erfurt, three different route options were investigated in a corridor that was approximately 20&#160;kilometre wide.<sup id="cite_ref-etr-2007-494_8-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-etr-2007-494-8">[8]</a></sup> The application documents for the line determination for the new line were submitted to the Federal Ministry of Transport in 1994 and the route was confirmed on 23&#160;June 1994 (another source: May 1994<sup id="cite_ref-bmv-1996-04-14_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bmv-1996-04-14-24">[24]</a></sup>) and the Federal Ministry of the Environment issued the decision.<sup id="cite_ref-etr-2007-494_8-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-etr-2007-494-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<p>The new line crosses the <a href="/wiki/Werra_Railway" class="mw-redirect" title="Werra Railway">Werra Railway</a> (<i>Werrabahn</i>) at kilometre 38.0 on the new line.<sup id="cite_ref-vde81-pfa-anl01_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vde81-pfa-anl01-25">[25]</a></sup> In the route selection, a connection of the new line with the Werra Railway between Grümpen and Rauenstein was considered.<sup id="cite_ref-vde81-pfa-anl01_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vde81-pfa-anl01-25">[25]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-freies-wort-2008-10-04_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-freies-wort-2008-10-04-26">[26]</a></sup> The cost of at least €150&#160;million was considered to be too high, so the plans were not pursued further.<sup id="cite_ref-freies-wort-2008-10-04_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-freies-wort-2008-10-04-26">[26]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Planning_approval_procedures">Planning approval procedures</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nuremberg%E2%80%93Erfurt_high-speed_railway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Planning approval procedures">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The planning procedures for the ten planning approval sections (including railway power lines) were initiated from December 1993. On 3&#160;May 1994 the first consultation procedure for the Zapfendorf–Grub am Forst section began, dealing with 8000 objections. By the end of 1994, nine out of ten procedures had been initiated, the last one being followed in 1995.<sup id="cite_ref-pbde-1995-01_11-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pbde-1995-01-11">[11]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-sz-1994-05-04_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sz-1994-05-04-27">[27]</a></sup> The first joint plan approval procedure for the section where the railway was "bundled" with the A&#160;71 was launched in January 1995. In 1995, the construction of the new bridge was expected to start in the same year.<sup id="cite_ref-bmv-1995-8_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bmv-1995-8-22">[22]</a></sup> Various complaints were brought against the project, which were also dealt with by the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Administrative_Court_(Germany)" title="Federal Administrative Court (Germany)">Federal Administrative Court</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-sz-1996-04-17-46_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sz-1996-04-17-46-28">[28]</a></sup></p>
<p>Due to the Transport Route Planning Acceleration Act (<i>Verkehrswegeplanungsbeschleunigungsgesetz</i>) adopted specifically for the new transport routes in the new federal states, it was possible to put the first planning approval decision for the Erfurt–<a href="/wiki/Arnstadt" title="Arnstadt">Arnstadt</a> section into effect at the end of 1994.<sup id="cite_ref-etr-2007-494_8-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-etr-2007-494-8">[8]</a></sup> The planning approval decisions for the new routes were adopted between 24&#160;May 1995 and 15&#160;April 1997.<sup id="cite_ref-bt-17-444_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bt-17-444-29">[29]</a></sup> In the middle of 1996, 75&#160;kilometres of the new line and 25&#160;kilometres of the rail power line were approved.<sup id="cite_ref-infob-1996-2-7_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-infob-1996-2-7-30">[30]</a></sup> The approvals were finalised in 1998 apart from the Erfurtstadt and <a href="/wiki/Bad_Staffelstein" title="Bad Staffelstein">Bad Staffelstein</a> sections. In the middle of 2007, the approvals were finalised for all sections.<sup id="cite_ref-etr-2007-494_8-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-etr-2007-494-8">[8]</a></sup> The planning approval decision for the southern section of the railway power line from the 19&#160;December 1995 lost its effect because the construction work had not commenced within the limited period of validity. As a result, a plan for the southern section of the railway power line to the Roth substation was reapplied for in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Construction_halt">Construction halt</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nuremberg%E2%80%93Erfurt_high-speed_railway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Construction halt">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The coalition agreement of the <a href="/wiki/First_Schr%C3%B6der_cabinet" title="First Schröder cabinet">SPD-Green coalition</a> of 20 October 1998 expressly provided for the examination of the Saxon-Franconian trunkline as an alternative to previous plans for the project.<sup id="cite_ref-koalitionsvertrag-1998_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-koalitionsvertrag-1998-32">[32]</a></sup> The coalition agreed on a review of the Nuremberg–Erfurt project.<sup id="cite_ref-handelsblatt-1999-116-6_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-handelsblatt-1999-116-6-33">[33]</a></sup></p>
<p>A construction site for a section of the new line was announced publicly on 30 March 1999. The Planungsgesellschaft Bahnbau Deutsche Einheit justified this in the absence of a financial agreement with the federal government. About DM 650&#160;million had previously been invested by the company in the project. The Federal Ministry of Transport and Communications emphasised that the project would be re-examined and that the results would be available within weeks.<sup id="cite_ref-sz-1999-03-30_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sz-1999-03-30-34">[34]</a></sup> At the end of May 1999, it became apparent that the project would not be realised in the planned form, especially due to the substitution of cheaper materials.<sup id="cite_ref-sz-1999-05-29_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sz-1999-05-29-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 7 July 1999, the then Federal Minister of Transport <a href="/wiki/Franz_M%C3%BCntefering" title="Franz Müntefering">Franz Müntefering</a> informed the Bavarian Minister-President <a href="/wiki/Edmund_Stoiber" title="Edmund Stoiber">Edmund Stoiber</a> that the new line and upgraded line would not be built for the time being. Because of the high cost of the project estimated to be DM 7 to 8 billion, other transport projects in Northern Bavaria, Saxony, Saxony-Anhalt and Thuringia would have been impossible. The scarce available funds would have to be used as efficiently as possible, according to Müntefering. In coordination with Deutsche Bahn, the Federal Government was pursuing a new strategy, in which "the emphasis would be on the maintenance and upgrading of existing routes". The section between Erfurt and Arnstadt would be "connected by a modified intermediate section to the existing line between Arnstadt and Saalfeld".<sup id="cite_ref-sz-1999-07-08_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sz-1999-07-08-4">[4]</a></sup> Trains at Arnstadt would be routed to Saalfeld via a connecting line to the <a href="/wiki/Gro%C3%9Fheringen%E2%80%93Saalfeld_railway" title="Großheringen–Saalfeld railway">Großheringen–Saalfeld railway</a> and would run from there to Nuremberg.<sup id="cite_ref-eri-1999-282_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eri-1999-282-36">[36]</a></sup> The journey time from Erfurt to Nuremberg would therefore decrease from 186 to 143&#160;minutes. An extension of the construction through the Thuringian Forest was kept open.<sup id="cite_ref-eri-1999-338_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eri-1999-338-37">[37]</a></sup> The Supervisory Board of Deutsche Bahn decided not to pursue the project any further.<sup id="cite_ref-sz-1999-07-12_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sz-1999-07-12-38">[38]</a></sup> Other alternative plans, however, were to use the Erfurt–Arnstadt–(Saalfeld) section with diesel regional cars.<sup id="cite_ref-infob-1999-1-12_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-infob-1999-1-12-39">[39]</a></sup> The Saxony-Anhalt Transport Minister Jürgen Heyer demanded to realisation of the new lew line over its full-length.<sup id="cite_ref-eri-1999-396_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eri-1999-396-40">[40]</a></sup> The proposals led to disputes within the then CDU/SPD state government in Thuringia. Minister-President Vogel (CDU) was not able to defend his position at a cabinet meeting, calling for a correction of the decision at the federal level.<sup id="cite_ref-sz-1999-07-10_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sz-1999-07-10-41">[41]</a></sup> It became an issue in the Thuringian Landtag election in 1999, in which Minister-President Vogel criticised the federal government repeatedly because of this decision.<sup id="cite_ref-sz-1999-07-12_38-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sz-1999-07-12-38">[38]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-sz-1999-08-21_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sz-1999-08-21-42">[42]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-sz-1999-07-06_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sz-1999-07-06-43">[43]</a></sup></p>
<p>At the beginning of 2000, plans were announced to continue the line progressively. The section between Erfurt and Ilmenau would be completed first and the need for an extension to Ebensfeld would be decided at a later stage and after further examination.<sup id="cite_ref-eri-2000-148_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eri-2000-148-44">[44]</a></sup> At a joint cabinet meeting at the end of March 2000, the state governments of Bavaria and Thuringia asked for an immediate increase in the construction activity on the line and for it to be finished by 2007. They declared their willingness to support the project with funds in the order of DM 50 million.<sup id="cite_ref-sz-2000-03-29-L8_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sz-2000-03-29-L8-45">[45]</a></sup></p>
<p>In mid-March 2002, the federal government raised the embargo on construction and announced that it wanted to quickly settle the financing with DB.<sup id="cite_ref-sz-2002-03-13-43_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sz-2002-03-13-43-46">[46]</a></sup> On10&#160;March 2002, the then Federal Chancellor <a href="/wiki/Gerhard_Schr%C3%B6der" title="Gerhard Schröder">Gerhard Schröder</a> announced the resumption of construction work. He said that the project had not been financed by the previous government and therefore had to be withdrawn.<sup id="cite_ref-spd-2002-03-10_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-spd-2002-03-10-47">[47]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Bahn" title="Deutsche Bahn">Deutsche Bahn</a> welcomed the decision.<sup id="cite_ref-eri-2002-211_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eri-2002-211-48">[48]</a></sup> At the end of February 2002, the then Minister of Transport <a href="/wiki/Kurt_Bodewig" title="Kurt Bodewig">Kurt Bodewig</a> had left the realisation of the project open.<sup id="cite_ref-mopo-2002-02-24_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mopo-2002-02-24-49">[49]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Operating_concept">Operating concept</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nuremberg%E2%80%93Erfurt_high-speed_railway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Operating concept">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="wikitable float-right">
<caption>Projected train numbers<sup id="cite_ref-br-2014-241_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-br-2014-241-50">[50]</a></sup></caption>
<tr>
<td>Year</td>
<td>Freight trains</td>
<td>passenger trains</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>1995</td>
<td>214</td>
<td>48</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>2010</td>
<td>169</td>
<td>40</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>2013</td>
<td>131</td>
<td>40</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>The new line is based on an operating concept with up to 137 trains each day and each way.</p>
<p>An hourly long-distance service each way with some additional trains and <a href="/wiki/Intercity-Express#ICE-Sprinter" title="Intercity-Express">ICE Sprinters</a> would be offered.<sup id="cite_ref-bt-16-13787_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bt-16-13787-51">[51]</a></sup> The Federal Government assumed an ICE service (Berlin–Munich) with about 20 passenger trains and 70 goods trains per day and direction.<sup id="cite_ref-bt-17-451_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bt-17-451-52">[52]</a></sup> In addition, an hourly service with a traffic class "below ICE standard" would be established.<sup id="cite_ref-bt-16-13787_51-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bt-16-13787-51">[51]</a></sup> The documents for the plan assessment of 1995 were as follows:</p>
<p>"The future operating program provides the following stops for long-distance (ICE) and regional (IR) networks:</p>
<ul>
<li>ICE stops: Nuremberg, Bamberg, Erfurt, additionally at the ends of the day in Erlangen and Coburg,</li>
<li>IR stops: Nuremberg, Erlangen, Bamberg, Coburg, Ilmenau, Erfurt."</li>
</ul>
<p>Coburg and Ilmenau were to be served by the ICE trains in the mornings and the evening according to the planning as of 2007. A stop in Coburg would extend the journey time of an ICE by ten minutes according to Deutsche Bahn.<sup id="cite_ref-np-coburg-2007-10-05_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-np-coburg-2007-10-05-53">[53]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-freies-wort-2007-09-03_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-freies-wort-2007-09-03-54">[54]</a></sup> According to the Federal Government in 2006, the operating concept envisaged nine daily train pairs serving Coburg.<sup id="cite_ref-bt-16-1379_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bt-16-1379-55">[55]</a></sup> As a guideline for the establishment of an ICE stop in Coburg an increase of at least 60 passengers per train would be required.<sup id="cite_ref-np-2008-07-18_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-np-2008-07-18-56">[56]</a></sup> A re-activation of the Werra Railway between Eisfeld and Coburg would be considered as part of an upgrade of Coburg as a south Thuringian ICE stop. The estimated costs were at least €60&#160;million.<sup id="cite_ref-freies-wort-2008-10-04_26-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-freies-wort-2008-10-04-26">[26]</a></sup></p>
<p>The proposed "Ilmenau-Wolfsberg" railway station was removed from the plans in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-eba-2011-11-22_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eba-2011-11-22-57">[57]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Ilm-Kreis" title="Ilm-Kreis">Ilm-Kreis</a> objected to this change of plan before the <i>Oberverwaltungsgericht</i> (state supreme administrative court). According to DB data, the necessary infrastructure could be retrofitted for passenger services subsequently.<sup id="cite_ref-fw-2012-07-12_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fw-2012-07-12-58">[58]</a></sup> According to the representatives of the state of Thuringia and the city of Ilmenau, plans for a regional service on the fast-line had not been pursued on their part. Special committees of the town of Ilmenau, according to a statement by Mayor Seeber at a citizens gathering, had turned against the planned Wümbach station and "opted for the development of the existing line".<sup id="cite_ref-freies-wort-2008-05-23_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-freies-wort-2008-05-23-59">[59]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Federal Government was expecting an increase of traffic of 1.8 million additional passengers per year after completion, generating almost 800 million passenger-kilometres. The forecast is based on a shift of approximately one million passenger journeys from the road and some 700,000 from the air (as of 2006). <a href="/wiki/DB_Netz" title="DB Netz">DB Netz</a> planned (as of 2002) to spend €37.3&#160;million per year after the opening of the line on a system for collecting data on train movements.<sup id="cite_ref-bt-16-1379_55-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bt-16-1379-55">[55]</a></sup></p>
<p>The roughly 80 freight trains per day and direction provided for in the federal transport plan for the route are to run mainly between 10 PM and 6&#160;AM. Between 6 AM and 22&#160;PM, one <a href="/wiki/Train_path" title="Train path">train path</a> each hour and each way would be available for freight traffic. In order to achieve the full freight transport capacity, upgrades at the <a href="/wiki/F%C3%BCrth_Hauptbahnhof" title="Fürth Hauptbahnhof">Fürth node</a> (including a planned freight train tunnel) and the provision of four tracks between Ebensfeld and Nuremberg would be necessary.<sup id="cite_ref-bt-16-13787_51-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bt-16-13787-51">[51]</a></sup></p>
<p>The traffic forecast for the Federal Transport Route Plan (<i>Bundesverkehrswegeplan</i>) 1992 provided for 24 passenger and 90 freight trains each day and each way on the new line in 2010. In the middle of 1994, Deutsche Bahn considered that there would be 24&#160;long-distance passenger trains and 55&#160;freight trains on the line. The segregation of fast and slow traffic (under the <i>Netz 21</i> project adopted in 1991) had not yet been considered.<sup id="cite_ref-bt-13-2130_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bt-13-2130-60">[60]</a></sup></p>
<p>Deutsche Bahn planned to have an ICE service running hourly on the line in 2030.<sup id="cite_ref-db-2015-03-18_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-db-2015-03-18-61">[61]</a></sup></p>
<p>An operations study was based on three possible freight train paths per hour in each direction while passenger services were operating.<sup id="cite_ref-weigand-2008_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-weigand-2008-62">[62]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span id="Ebensfeld–Erfurt_new_line"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Ebensfeld.E2.80.93Erfurt_new_line">Ebensfeld–Erfurt new line</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nuremberg%E2%80%93Erfurt_high-speed_railway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Ebensfeld–Erfurt new line">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The new line begins north of Ebensfeld near the 20.4 kilometre-mark on the Bamberg–Lichtenfels line and ends in Erfurt at the entrance signals of the station.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup></p>
<p>It is 107&#160;kilometres long, of which 34&#160;kilometres is located in <a href="/wiki/Bavaria" title="Bavaria">Bavaria</a> and 73&#160;kilometres in <a href="/wiki/Thuringia" title="Thuringia">Thuringia</a>. The line runs at a normal maximum grade of 1.25%, although parts have grades of up to 2.0%, and curves have a normal minimum radius of 6,300&#160;metres and an absolute minimum radius of 3,700&#160;metres.<sup id="cite_ref-pbde-1995-01_11-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pbde-1995-01-11">[11]</a></sup> Normal passing loops are 25,000&#160;metres long and their minimum length is 22,500&#160;metres.<sup id="cite_ref-brueckenbau-2009-99_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-brueckenbau-2009-99-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
<p>It passes through the <a href="/wiki/Thuringian_Forest" title="Thuringian Forest">Thuringian Forest</a> between Truckenthal and Ilmenau over a length of 27.4&#160;kilometres and rises temporarily to a height of around 600&#160;metres above sea level. This section contains nine tunnels with a total length of 22.7&#160;kilometres (83% of the tunnels by length on the line). The intervening valleys are crossed by nine bridges.<sup id="cite_ref-koennings-1999_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-koennings-1999-19">[19]</a></sup> In a 23&#160;kilometres long section built alongside the A&#160;71, the line is largely confined to a 40-metre-wide strip of land.<sup id="cite_ref-pbde-1996_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pbde-1996-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<p>The design speed is 300&#160;km/h.<sup id="cite_ref-pbde-1995-01_11-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pbde-1995-01-11">[11]</a></sup> The planned maximum speed was initially 250&#160;km/h<sup id="cite_ref-pbde-1995-01_11-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pbde-1995-01-11">[11]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bmv-1997-04-19_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bmv-1997-04-19-64">[64]</a></sup> and was later raised to 300&#160;km/h. One source from 2009 again refers to a planned maximum speed of 250&#160;km/h.<sup id="cite_ref-brueckenbau-2009-99_13-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-brueckenbau-2009-99-13">[13]</a></sup> For the regional services south of Coburg that have operated since 2016, the maximum permissible speed has been reduced to 250&#160;km/h.<sup id="cite_ref-stmi-2016-06-24_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stmi-2016-06-24-65">[65]</a></sup></p>
<p>More than fifty percent of the length of the route consists of civil engineering works—a new record for German high-speed railways.<sup id="cite_ref-etr-2007-502_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-etr-2007-502-66">[66]</a></sup> The planned 22 tunnels have a total length of 41&#160;kilometres, the two longest are the 8,314 m-long Blessberg Tunnel at 8,326&#160;metres<sup id="cite_ref-plan_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-plan-67">[67]</a></sup> and the Silberberg Tunnel at 7,407&#160;metres.<sup id="cite_ref-plan1_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-plan1-68">[68]</a></sup> Its 29 viaducts have a total length of 12&#160;km; the longest is the 1,681 m-long Ilm Viaduct. In addition another 46 road and path crossings are planned.<sup id="cite_ref-np-coburg-2007-09-01_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-np-coburg-2007-09-01-69">[69]</a></sup> The ruling maximum gradient is 1.25%. In four short sections, this was increased to 2.0% to reduce capital costs.<sup id="cite_ref-bt-16-13787_51-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bt-16-13787-51">[51]</a></sup> Such sections were not planned until detailed planning began in spring 1994,<sup id="cite_ref-vde8-ba211-anl1.2_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vde8-ba211-anl1.2-70">[70]</a></sup> but in mid-1994 seven such sections were planned with longitudinal grades between 1.778 und 2.00&#160;percent over a length of 400&#160;metres to 1.1&#160;kilometres.<sup id="cite_ref-vde8-ba22-anl1.2_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vde8-ba22-anl1.2-71">[71]</a></sup></p>
<p>The power supply was connected to the <a href="/wiki/Traction_power_network" title="Traction power network">traction power network</a> by means of two new spur lines running via three new substations at <a href="/wiki/Schalkau" title="Schalkau">Roth</a>, Ilmenau and Eischleben.<sup id="cite_ref-pbde-1995-01_11-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pbde-1995-01-11">[11]</a></sup> The existing Ebensfeld substation was expanded for the power supply of the new line. There was no equalisation of the earth masses, which meant that about 16 million cubic metres of earth was deposited at 24<sup id="cite_ref-etr-2007-502_66-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-etr-2007-502-66">[66]</a></sup> landfill sites. Near Masserberg. for example, 1.8&#160;million cubic metres was dumped covering an area of 54.8&#160;<a href="/wiki/Hectare" title="Hectare">hectares</a>, with a maximum height of 27&#160;metres.</p>
<p>The permanent surface requirements of the new line are around 435&#160;hectares. In the construction phase, a total of around 1200&#160;hectares was required. Around 990&#160;hectares has been provided for environmental compensation areas.<sup id="cite_ref-pbde-1996_12-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pbde-1996-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span id="Erfurt–Ilmenau_route_description"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Erfurt.E2.80.93Ilmenau_route_description">Erfurt–Ilmenau route description</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nuremberg%E2%80%93Erfurt_high-speed_railway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Erfurt–Ilmenau route description">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>From Erfurt station, the route runs west on the northern side of the <a href="/wiki/Gera_(river)" title="Gera (river)">Gera</a> valley, parallel to the tracks of the <a href="/wiki/Halle%E2%80%93Bebra_railway" title="Halle–Bebra railway">Halle–Bebra railway</a> (Thuringian Railway). It separates from that line before Erfurt-Bischleben in order to cross over the river and a road and enter the Augustaburg Tunnel. After the tunnel, the line turns south and parallels the <a href="/wiki/Bundesautobahn_71" title="Bundesautobahn 71">Autobahn 71</a>. First, it runs on the western side of the Autobahn and crosses the <a href="/wiki/Apfelst%C3%A4dt_(Gera)" title="Apfelstädt (Gera)">Apfelstädt</a>, a state road and the Thuringian Railway on the Apfelstädt viaduct. This is followed by the Gera Viaduct at Ichtershausen and crossings of the <a href="/wiki/Bundesautobahn_4" title="Bundesautobahn 4">A&#160;4</a> at the Erfurt interchange, the A&#160;71 in a cutting and the Gera again. As far as <a href="/wiki/Wipfratal" title="Wipfratal">Neuroda</a>, it is then built on the western side of the A&#160;71. After passing under the A&#160;71 through the Sandberg Tunnel, it then follow a separate route. In the following section of about seven kilometres, it passses over the Wümbach Viaduct to the new Ilmenau-Wolfsberg overtaking loops. On the way to Ilmenau, the line passes through the Thuringian Forest via nine tunnels with a total length of more than 22&#160;kilometres.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Construction">Construction</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nuremberg%E2%80%93Erfurt_high-speed_railway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Construction">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:%C3%9Cbf_Theuern_Truckenthal.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/%C3%9Cbf_Theuern_Truckenthal.jpg/220px-%C3%9Cbf_Theuern_Truckenthal.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/%C3%9Cbf_Theuern_Truckenthal.jpg/330px-%C3%9Cbf_Theuern_Truckenthal.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/%C3%9Cbf_Theuern_Truckenthal.jpg/440px-%C3%9Cbf_Theuern_Truckenthal.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="667" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:%C3%9Cbf_Theuern_Truckenthal.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Earthworks for the future Theuern relief loops, view from the facility over the Truckenthal towards the Bleßberg</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Einschnitt-Kohlitschberg.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Einschnitt-Kohlitschberg.jpg/220px-Einschnitt-Kohlitschberg.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Einschnitt-Kohlitschberg.jpg/330px-Einschnitt-Kohlitschberg.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Einschnitt-Kohlitschberg.jpg/440px-Einschnitt-Kohlitschberg.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5324" data-file-height="3549" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Einschnitt-Kohlitschberg.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
View in July 2012 to the highest point of the route from the southern portal of the Rehberg Tunnel towards the Dunkel Viaduct, the Kohlitschberg cutting, the Gruben Viaduct and the Goldberg Tunnel</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Tunnel-Reitersberg-Schienentransport.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Tunnel-Reitersberg-Schienentransport.jpg/220px-Tunnel-Reitersberg-Schienentransport.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Tunnel-Reitersberg-Schienentransport.jpg/330px-Tunnel-Reitersberg-Schienentransport.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Tunnel-Reitersberg-Schienentransport.jpg/440px-Tunnel-Reitersberg-Schienentransport.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5616" data-file-height="3744" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Tunnel-Reitersberg-Schienentransport.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
November 2013, rail track transport vehicle near Reitersberg Tunnel</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:NBS-Ebensfeld-02.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/NBS-Ebensfeld-02.jpg/220px-NBS-Ebensfeld-02.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/NBS-Ebensfeld-02.jpg/330px-NBS-Ebensfeld-02.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/NBS-Ebensfeld-02.jpg/440px-NBS-Ebensfeld-02.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5616" data-file-height="3744" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:NBS-Ebensfeld-02.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
New line north of Ebensfeld, with a construction track leading towards Bamberg (2016)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>With the ceremonial foundation of a bridge of the Rudisleben–<a href="/wiki/Kirchheim,_Thuringia" title="Kirchheim, Thuringia">Kirchheim</a> <a href="/wiki/Landesstra%C3%9Fe" title="Landesstraße">state road</a> over the future Eischleben relief loops, work on the new and upgraded line began on 16&#160;April 1996.<sup id="cite_ref-ek-2008-11-40_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ek-2008-11-40-5">[5]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-infob-1996-2-7_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-infob-1996-2-7-30">[30]</a></sup> At the same time, the construction of the <a href="/wiki/Bundesautobahn_71" title="Bundesautobahn 71">A71</a> (VDE Project No.&#160;16) commenced.<sup id="cite_ref-bmv-1997-04-19_64-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bmv-1997-04-19-64">[64]</a></sup> The first groundbreaking was carried out by the Federal Minister of Transport, <a href="/wiki/Matthias_Wissmann" title="Matthias Wissmann">Matthias Wissmann</a>, the Thuringian Minister President, <a href="/wiki/Bernhard_Vogel_(politician)" title="Bernhard Vogel (politician)">Bernhard Vogel</a> and the Bavarian Minister of Economic Affairs, <a href="/wiki/Otto_Wiesheu" title="Otto Wiesheu">Otto Wiesheu</a>, who gave speeches despite loud protests by environmentalists.<sup id="cite_ref-sz-1996-04-17-46_28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sz-1996-04-17-46-28">[28]</a></sup> Among the guests was Heinz Dürr, the head of DB at that time.<sup id="cite_ref-infob-1996-2-1_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-infob-1996-2-1-72">[72]</a></sup></p>
<p>The construction work concentrated first on the 23&#160;kilometre-long section "bundled" with the A&#160;71 between Erfurt and Arnstadt. Construction of the almost 37&#160;kilometre-long section between Erfurt and Ilmenau began in April&#160;1996 and was almost completed in 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-ek-2008-11-40_5-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ek-2008-11-40-5">[5]</a></sup> These included the Augustaburg, Behringen and Sandberg tunnels as well as the 1,100&#160;metre-long Gera Viaduct at Ichtershausen and the 570&#160;metre-long Wümbach Viaduct.</p>
<p>At the beginning of December 1998, a newspaper reported that the Federal Ministry of Transport had issued an order to stop work on the southern part of the new line so that the work program could be examined. The northern section that was being built along with the A&#160;71 was not affected.<sup id="cite_ref-ek-1999-2-11_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ek-1999-2-11-73">[73]</a></sup> After the Federal Ministry of Transport initially stopped pre-construction activities in July 1999 as a result of tight budgets, some work, mainly consisting of pre-construction work, was carried out in 2003 and 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-ek-2008-11-40_5-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ek-2008-11-40-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<p>The construction of the approximately seven kilometre-long section integrating the new line into the Erfurt node began in 2001.<sup id="cite_ref-db-2002-16_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-db-2002-16-74">[74]</a></sup> In 2005, work started on the Stelzen intermediate access tunnel to the Bleßberg tunnel and approximately 20&#160;kilometres of access roads were built in the Thuringian Forest.<sup id="cite_ref-etr-2007-502_66-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-etr-2007-502-66">[66]</a></sup> The first construction phase and the associated platforms were commissioned at Erfurt station in November 2005. At Coburg, work commenced at the end of 2005 on the Itz Viaduct, the neighbouring construction of the shell of the 221&#160;metre-long tunnel of the Dörfles-Esbach connecting curve and a road crossing.</p>
<p>The project has been supervised and managed by <a href="/wiki/DB_ProjektBau" title="DB ProjektBau">DB ProjektBau</a> since 2003. From 2000 to 2002, the project was managed by <i>DB Projektverkehrbau</i>, the planning company of Bahnbau Deutsche Einheit.</p>
<p>Construction began on the Grümpen Viaduct, including a 270-metre-long arch, in June 2006. This was followed by the commencement of the Froschgrundsee bridge with the same span in the autumn. At the end of 2006, contracts were awarded for the Truckenthal and Pöpelholz viaducts. In addition, construction of a two kilometre-long section of line connecting the Itz Viaduct towards Erfurt and the 4300&#160;metre-long Bleßberg tunnel commenced. On 30 March 2008, the work on the Bleßberg tunnel lead to the discovery of a large limestone cave, the Bleiberberg cave.</p>
<p>Preparatory work started on the construction of the Ilm Viaduct in April/May 2007. At the end of May 2007, Deutsche Bahn issued a European-wide advertisement for the construction of a one-kilometre section of the Tragberg Tunnel<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> and the construction of the Füllbach Bridge began.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> In the Coburg area, construction had been under way since September 2007 near Grub am Forst and Dörfles-Esbach, as well as the Froschgrundsee and Pöpelholz viaducts.</p>
<p>Work on the Müß Tunnel commenced on 29&#160;February 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-db-2008-02-29_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-db-2008-02-29-77">[77]</a></sup> At the beginning of April 2008, Deutsche Bahn called tenders for the construction of the Masserberg, Rehberg, Kulch and Lichtenholz tunnels and the Dunkel, Reh and Mühlbach viaducts in September and November 2008 respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-ted-2008.2FS63-085579_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ted-2008.2FS63-085579-78">[78]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ted-2008.2FS63-085578_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ted-2008.2FS63-085578-79">[79]</a></sup> By the end of 2008, all major civil engineering projects<sup id="cite_ref-etr-2007-502_66-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-etr-2007-502-66">[66]</a></sup> and the construction of all "construction time-determining civil engineering works" would be awarded.<sup id="cite_ref-db-2008-02-29_77-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-db-2008-02-29-77">[77]</a></sup> At the end of January 2009, the DB advertised tenders for the section from track-kilometre 15.8 to 18.0 (near Coburg) and the first 1.8&#160;kilometre of the Coburg southern connection, each including one tunnel.<sup id="cite_ref-ted-2009.2FS_19-027336_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ted-2009.2FS_19-027336-80">[80]</a></sup> The invitation to tender for the integration of the line into the Erfurt node followed in July 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-ted-197803-2009-DE_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ted-197803-2009-DE-81">[81]</a></sup> This was to be carried out in nine stages with train operations continuing and is scheduled to be completed in 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup></p>
<p>According to Deutsche Bahn, the already built structures have already been included in the regular maintenance program in order to ensure their functionality at the opening of the line.<sup id="cite_ref-freies-wort-2007-07-17_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-freies-wort-2007-07-17-83">[83]</a></sup> Early operations on the section between Erfurt and Ilmenau and further modifications of the project were proposed.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> Deutsche Bahn rejected early operations on the line. On the one hand, such regional services had not been ordered by the State of Thuringia; on the other hand, the safety and control technology that would have had to be installed would have become obsolete when the entire line was opened and would have had to be replaced. The costs would have exceeded the benefits.<sup id="cite_ref-freies-wort-2007-07-16_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-freies-wort-2007-07-16-85">[85]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2008, work was carried out on five bridges and tunnels of the new line.<sup id="cite_ref-bt-17-444_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bt-17-444-29">[29]</a></sup> Höhnberg Tunnel was officially the last of the large projects to commence on the new line, with work starting on 30&#160;September 2011.</p>
<p>Near Püchitz, around 20,000 pieces were found at the largest North Bavarian site of the <a href="/wiki/Linear_Pottery_culture" title="Linear Pottery culture">Linear Pottery culture</a> during archaeological excavations on the course of the new line up to mid-2010.<sup id="cite_ref-np-2010-08-12_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-np-2010-08-12-86">[86]</a></sup></p>
<p>The permanent track and the overhead line on the northern section between Ilmenau and Erfurt would be built between August 2010 and November 2013,<sup id="cite_ref-ted-2009.2FS_180-258547_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ted-2009.2FS_180-258547-87">[87]</a></sup> on the middle section between Coburg and Ilmenau between December 2012 and December 2015<sup id="cite_ref-ted-2011.2FS_234-379636_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ted-2011.2FS_234-379636-88">[88]</a></sup> and on the southern section between Bad Staffelstein and Coburg between January 2013 and December 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-ted-2011.2FS_34-055237_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ted-2011.2FS_34-055237-89">[89]</a></sup> The contracts, which comprise the fixed track, including the foundations of the masts for the overhead line and wind and noise protection equipment, were let for the approximately 44 kilometre-long middle section for around €104 million<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> and the approximately 22 kilometre-long southern section for around €60 million.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup></p>
<p>The construction of superstructure and catenary in the 32.5&#160;kilometre-long section between Erfurt and Ilmenau officially began on 9&#160;September 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-db-2010-09-09_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-db-2010-09-09-92">[92]</a></sup> €110 million was allocated for the two-year construction work.<sup id="cite_ref-otz-2010-09-09_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-otz-2010-09-09-93">[93]</a></sup></p>
<p>Tunneling of the five still outstanding tunnels began during 2011 and the work in the Ebensfeld/Unterleiterbach area began in the first half of 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup></p>
<p>Around 1,500 employees were employed on the new line at the end of 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-newstix-2011-11-29_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-newstix-2011-11-29-95">[95]</a></sup></p>
<p>The last tunnel of the new line of the VDE&#160;8 transport projects, the Höhnberg Tunnel was broken through on 25&#160;August 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-db-2012-08-03_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-db-2012-08-03-96">[96]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:NBS-Ebensfeld-Erfurt-L%C3%BCckenschlussfeier-01.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/NBS-Ebensfeld-Erfurt-L%C3%BCckenschlussfeier-01.jpg/220px-NBS-Ebensfeld-Erfurt-L%C3%BCckenschlussfeier-01.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/NBS-Ebensfeld-Erfurt-L%C3%BCckenschlussfeier-01.jpg/330px-NBS-Ebensfeld-Erfurt-L%C3%BCckenschlussfeier-01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/NBS-Ebensfeld-Erfurt-L%C3%BCckenschlussfeier-01.jpg/440px-NBS-Ebensfeld-Erfurt-L%C3%BCckenschlussfeier-01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5616" data-file-height="3744" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:NBS-Ebensfeld-Erfurt-L%C3%BCckenschlussfeier-01.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
End of the Müß tunnel on 9&#160;September&#160;2016</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In June 2013, the Dörfles-Esbach connecting curve was connected to the existing network, in order to be able to carry the rails for the construction of the line, among other things.<sup id="cite_ref-ct-2013-06-19_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ct-2013-06-19-97">[97]</a></sup> The rails of the new line came from several large German track manufacturers and some were carried by goods trains on the lines from Coburg<sup id="cite_ref-fw-2014-02-27_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fw-2014-02-27-98">[98]</a></sup> and Erfurt.<sup id="cite_ref-ta-2014-08-27_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ta-2014-08-27-99">[99]</a></sup> At the end of November 2014 Deutsche Bahn announced that all 29&#160;bridges on the new line had been completed.<sup id="cite_ref-db-2014-11-25_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-db-2014-11-25-100">[100]</a></sup></p>
<p>In September 2014, the railway engineering equipment began working on the route, mainly to lay power cables. According to Deutsche Bahn AG, the work would be completed in September 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> In 2015 and 2016, installation of rail equipment (in particular ETCS and telecommunications) would follow.<sup id="cite_ref-ek-2008-11-40_5-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ek-2008-11-40-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<p>The construction work on the line is to be completed in early 2017 and trial operations are planned from mid-2017.<sup id="cite_ref-ta-2014-12-4_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ta-2014-12-4-102">[102]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Commissioning">Commissioning</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nuremberg%E2%80%93Erfurt_high-speed_railway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Commissioning">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In February 2016, the first section of the new line was completed with a top permitted speed of 20&#160;km/h.<sup id="cite_ref-np-2016-02-16_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-np-2016-02-16-103">[103]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-eri-2016-224_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eri-2016-224-104">[104]</a></sup></p>
<p>The first trials were due to take place in May 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-ft-2015-07-15_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ft-2015-07-15-105">[105]</a></sup> According to information supplied by DB in July 2015, the deadline for commissioning is testing, but achievable, so long as no major delays occur. The connection of the new line near Bamberg was made more difficult by a complaint of a nature protection organisation.<sup id="cite_ref-otz-2015-07-29_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-otz-2015-07-29-106">[106]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Accidents">Accidents</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nuremberg%E2%80%93Erfurt_high-speed_railway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Accidents">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<ul>
<li>On 24 July 2008, the arch of the Truckenthal Viaduct collapsed while under construction due to a technical defect in an auxiliary support. Nobody was hurt. The construction work was subsequently discontinued, a column including an arch section was demolished on 28&#160;January 2009 and then removed.</li>
<li>During the building of the Ilm Viaduct on 1 September 2008, a construction worker was killed and three were injured (in some cases badly) as scaffolding with a reinforced cage collapsed during an <a href="/wiki/Incremental_launch" title="Incremental launch">incremental launch</a>.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Outlook">Outlook</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nuremberg%E2%80%93Erfurt_high-speed_railway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Outlook">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:D%C3%B6rfles-Esbach-Verbindungskurve-01.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/D%C3%B6rfles-Esbach-Verbindungskurve-01.jpg/170px-D%C3%B6rfles-Esbach-Verbindungskurve-01.jpg" width="170" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/D%C3%B6rfles-Esbach-Verbindungskurve-01.jpg/255px-D%C3%B6rfles-Esbach-Verbindungskurve-01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/D%C3%B6rfles-Esbach-Verbindungskurve-01.jpg/340px-D%C3%B6rfles-Esbach-Verbindungskurve-01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3744" data-file-height="5616" /></a>

</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Tunnel-Eierberge-Tunnelreinigungszug.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Tunnel-Eierberge-Tunnelreinigungszug.jpg/220px-Tunnel-Eierberge-Tunnelreinigungszug.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Tunnel-Eierberge-Tunnelreinigungszug.jpg/330px-Tunnel-Eierberge-Tunnelreinigungszug.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Tunnel-Eierberge-Tunnelreinigungszug.jpg/440px-Tunnel-Eierberge-Tunnelreinigungszug.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5616" data-file-height="3744" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Tunnel-Eierberge-Tunnelreinigungszug.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Tunnel cleaning train in front of the Eierberge tunnel, June&#160; 2016</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The planned date of commissioning has been postponed several times. Thus, in July 1997, the commissioning of the new line was still expected in 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-bmv-1997-04-19_64-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bmv-1997-04-19-64">[64]</a></sup> In December 2006, the Federal Government and Deutsche Bahn AG announced that the new line would be completed in 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-eurailpress-2006-12-20_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eurailpress-2006-12-20-107">[107]</a></sup> In May 2006, the opening year was given as 2020 in a response to a parliamentary question from the Green Party, although the Federal Minister of Transport <a href="/wiki/Wolfgang_Tiefensee" title="Wolfgang Tiefensee">Wolfgang Tiefensee</a> indicated at the opening of the Nürnberg-Ingolstadt high-speed line, that the line would be opened in 2016/2017. At the end of 2007 the Süddeutsche Zeitung reported that the line would not be completed until 2041.<sup id="cite_ref-sz-2007-12-02_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sz-2007-12-02-108">[108]</a></sup> Later, it became known that 2041 had been used in a meeting of the board of directors to refer to the completion date of the upgraded line between Fürth and Ebensfeld. The new line is still planned to be completed by 2017 at the latest.<sup id="cite_ref-np-2008-01-18_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-np-2008-01-18-109">[109]</a></sup> Commissioning is now scheduled for the timetable change on 8&#160;December 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-ek-2008-11-40_5-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ek-2008-11-40-5">[5]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-fw-2008-09-16_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fw-2008-09-16-6">[6]</a></sup> According to information from mid-2015, this date is tight, but it can be kept.<sup id="cite_ref-otz-2015-07-29_106-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-otz-2015-07-29-106">[106]</a></sup> €29&#160;million were provided for the new line from the <i>Konjunkturpaket&#160;I</i> ("stimulus package I").<sup id="cite_ref-bmvbs-2009-07-29_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bmvbs-2009-07-29-110">[110]</a></sup> In December 2006, a parliamentary support group was founded called <i>Vollendung des Verkehrsprojektes Deutsche Einheit Nr.&#160;8</i> ("Completion of German Unity transport project No. 8"), comprising over twenty Bundestag deputies. The parliamentarians were keen to accelerate the completion of the line.<sup id="cite_ref-eurailpress-2006-12-20_107-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eurailpress-2006-12-20-107">[107]</a></sup> In April 2007, Transport Minister Tiefensee confirmed with the support group that the line would be completied by 2016,<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> but in May 2008 the parliamentarians announced 2017 as the completion date in a press release.<sup id="cite_ref-ParlUnterst.C3.BCtzer2008_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ParlUnterst.C3.BCtzer2008-112">[112]</a></sup></p>
<p>The symbolic closing of the gap was celebrated on 9 September 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-db-2016-09-09_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-db-2016-09-09-113">[113]</a></sup> High-speed runs were due to begin on 17 October 2016. Trials will begin at 160&#160;km/h and will be increased in 20-km/h increments until ultimately 330&#160;km/h is achieved.<sup id="cite_ref-ta-2016-10-13_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ta-2016-10-13-114">[114]</a></sup> The runs will take about three weeks and the data will be evaluated over several months.<sup id="cite_ref-np-2016-10-20_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-np-2016-10-20-115">[115]</a></sup> ETCS test runs are to follow later.<sup id="cite_ref-ta-2016-10-13_114-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ta-2016-10-13-114">[114]</a></sup></p>
<p>Further operational testing, acceptance and approval are to take place in 2017 so that regular services can begin at the timetable change in December 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-ek-2008-11-40_5-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ek-2008-11-40-5">[5]</a></sup> According to Deutsche Bahn, the possible building technology for the fastest possible realisation of the line were exhausted. An additional base of works in the cente of the line would not have resulted in a significantly earlier commissioning.<sup id="cite_ref-bt-16-13787_51-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bt-16-13787-51">[51]</a></sup></p>
<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional">
