<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Operations">Operations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nuremberg%E2%80%93Erfurt_high-speed_railway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Operations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>As a result of the overall project including the newly built line and the upgraded line, the volume of passenger traffic is expected to increase by about 3.1&#160;million trips per year and freight traffic is expected to increase by 2.9&#160;billion tonne-kilometres.<sup id="cite_ref-bt-17-4410_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bt-17-4410-116">[116]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Passenger_traffic">Passenger traffic</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nuremberg%E2%80%93Erfurt_high-speed_railway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Passenger traffic">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The following passenger services are to operate via the new line:<sup id="cite_ref-db-2013-08-26_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-db-2013-08-26-117">[117]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-etr-64-33_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-etr-64-33-118">[118]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li>Berlin–Halle–Erfurt–Nuremberg–Munich (line 28.1, every two hours in hour 1)</li>
<li>(north Germany–) Berlin–Leipzig–Erfurt–Nuremberg–Munich (line 28.2, every two hours in hour 2)</li>
<li>Berlin–Halle–Erfurt–Nuremberg–Munich (ICE Sprinter line 29, three train pairs per day)</li>
</ul>
<p>In regional transport, a Regional-Express service is to be established running over the new line on the Nuremberg–Coburg–Sonneberg (state border) route. Up to seven train pairs per day are foreseen.<sup id="cite_ref-stmi-2016-06-24_65-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stmi-2016-06-24-65">[65]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ted-457927_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ted-457927-119">[119]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ft-2015-12-30_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ft-2015-12-30-120">[120]</a></sup></p>
<p>Between Nuremberg and Erfurt the journey time of three hours (2014) will be shortened to about an hour.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> The travel times between Berlin/Leipzig/Dresden and Nuremberg/Munich will be shortened by about one and a half to two hours during the same period.<sup id="cite_ref-dbpb-2014-4_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dbpb-2014-4-122">[122]</a></sup></p>
<p>A node of the <a href="/wiki/Clock-face_scheduling" title="Clock-face scheduling">clock-face timetable</a> is to be established at Erfurt station. Trains will be scheduled to arrive and depart every hour between the minutes of 24 and 36 and regional services will be scheduled to arrive and depart between the minutes of 16 and 44.<sup id="cite_ref-haedrich-2012-06-08_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-haedrich-2012-06-08-123">[123]</a></sup> With the start of passenger services on the new line, Naumburg, Jena, Saalfeld and Lichtenfels will lose their long-distance services.<sup id="cite_ref-db-2013-08-26_117-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-db-2013-08-26-117">[117]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Freight_traffic">Freight traffic</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nuremberg%E2%80%93Erfurt_high-speed_railway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Freight traffic">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>According to data from 2016, <a href="/wiki/DB_Cargo" title="DB Cargo">DB Cargo</a> expects to have sufficient ETCS-equipped locomotives to be able to run freight traffic on the high-speed line. A forecast then expects a maximum of 20 freight train pairs per day; with an upgrade of the existing stretch to Erlangen to four tracks, it would be able to run 30 freight train pairs per day. From 2025, 60 freight trains would operate daily over the new line. 140 freight trains are to be operated over the existing line ("Saalbahn"). For a freight train from Halle (Saale) to Nuremberg, the price for operating a train will be €2180 via the new line and €985 via the current line (as of 2016). The route over the high-speed line is 30&#160;kilometres shorter and less steep (a maximum grade of 2.0% instead of 2.7%).<sup id="cite_ref-otz-2016-06-10_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-otz-2016-06-10-124">[124]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Technology">Technology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nuremberg%E2%80%93Erfurt_high-speed_railway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Technology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Feste-Fahrbahn-Boegl.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Feste-Fahrbahn-Boegl.jpg/220px-Feste-Fahrbahn-Boegl.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Feste-Fahrbahn-Boegl.jpg/330px-Feste-Fahrbahn-Boegl.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Feste-Fahrbahn-Boegl.jpg/440px-Feste-Fahrbahn-Boegl.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5616" data-file-height="3744" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Feste-Fahrbahn-Boegl.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Bögl slab track system at the Goldisthal information centre</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The high-speed is intended exclusively for electric traction and is equipped with class Re&#160;330 <a href="/wiki/Overhead_line" title="Overhead line">overhead line</a>.</p>
<p>The new line will be built using <a href="/wiki/Slab_track" class="mw-redirect" title="Slab track">slab track</a>, although overtaking tracks and connections to the existing network are being built with conventional ballast.<sup id="cite_ref-etr-2007-494_8-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-etr-2007-494-8">[8]</a></sup> The distance between track centres will be 4.70&#160;metre<sup id="cite_ref-pbde-1995-01_11-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pbde-1995-01-11">[11]</a></sup> and the planning width of a straight section of track is 13.30&#160;metres. In the Thuringian section of the line, the track distance was adjusted to 4.50&#160;metre in a change of plans in 1998. The planning width was reduced to 12.10&#160;metres and the cross-section of the tunnel was reduced from 101 to 92&#160;square metres.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup> The additional cost of maintaining the larger track distances in Bavaria was estimated by the <a href="/wiki/Bundesrechnungshof" title="Bundesrechnungshof">Federal Audit Office</a> in 2014 to be at least €35 million. The Federal Railway Authority (<i>Eisenbahn-Bundesamt</i>—EBA) stated that in Bavaria, in contrast to Thuringia, changes to the planning approval decisions would have led to a risk of third-party objections. The Federal Audit Office considered this to be inaccurate, since the reduction in the distance between the tracks in Bavaria would have reduced the extent to which the environment was affected.<sup id="cite_ref-br-2014-239_126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-br-2014-239-126">[126]</a></sup> Near the Augustaburg tunnel, the track distance is reduced to 4.00&#160;metres.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup></p>
<p>The track changes are designed for a branch speed of 130&#160;km/h. The distances of the overtaking facilities were determined in a study conducted by the company and are measured according to the planned operating program.<sup id="cite_ref-etr-2007-494_8-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-etr-2007-494-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/European_Train_Control_System#Level_2" title="European Train Control System">ETCS Level 2</a> is being deployed on the Ebensfeld–Erfurt–Halle/Leipzig route without trackside signals and with no signal-based fallback for the first time in Germany.<sup id="cite_ref-db-2007-09-06_128-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-db-2007-09-06-128">[128]</a></sup> An ETCS line centre for the high-speed line is planned in Unterleiterbach.<sup id="cite_ref-eri-2016-76_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eri-2016-76-129">[129]</a></sup> It was still planned in 2014 to upgrade ETCS to <a href="/wiki/European_Train_Control_System#Baseline_3" title="European Train Control System">Baseline 3</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-db-netz-2014-04_130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-db-netz-2014-04-130">[130]</a></sup> Meanwhile, (2015), it is planned to operate the line under the SRS&#160;2.3.0&#160;D and to upgrade the line to Baseline 3 later.</p>
<p>As a fallback to ETCS, an intermittent train control system (<a href="/wiki/Punktf%C3%B6rmige_Zugbeeinflussung" title="Punktförmige Zugbeeinflussung">Punktförmige Zugbeeinflussung</a>) was modelled, which would allow operations outside of stations with turnouts at speeds of up 160&#160;km/h. Procedures were also developed for dealing with a malfunctioning GSM-R <a href="/wiki/Base_transceiver_station" title="Base transceiver station">Base transceiver station</a>, so that trains can be run through.<sup id="cite_ref-etr-61-4-10_131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-etr-61-4-10-131">[131]</a></sup></p>
<p>Various solutions were investigated for the realisation of the ban on passenger and freight trains operating through tunnels at the same time and a special system was conceived, which transmits permissions at the entrance gateways to tunnels, as long as certain criteria are met. For this purpose, configuration data (e.g. tunnel areas) and rules for permissible and impermissible adjustments as well as train categories, which have different characteristics (e.g. axle pattern and ETCS train category), have been developed. A corresponding system was in the final phase of development in the middle of 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-etr-61-4-10_131-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-etr-61-4-10-131">[131]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-deine-bahn-2015-6-12_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-deine-bahn-2015-6-12-132">[132]</a></sup></p>
<p>26 <a href="/wiki/GSM-R" title="GSM-R">GSM-R</a> <a href="/wiki/Base_transceiver_station" title="Base transceiver station">base transceiver stations</a> and 31 <a href="/wiki/Repeater" title="Repeater">repeaters</a> are provided for voice and data communication.<sup id="cite_ref-eri-2016-76_129-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eri-2016-76-129">[129]</a></sup></p>
<p>The route is part of the trans-European high-speed railway network as defined in the <a href="/wiki/Technical_Specification_for_Interoperability" class="mw-redirect" title="Technical Specification for Interoperability">Technical Specification for Interoperability</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-etr-2007-494_8-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-etr-2007-494-8">[8]</a></sup> The route is to be controlled by seven <a href="/wiki/Electronic_interlocking" class="mw-redirect" title="Electronic interlocking">electronic interlockings</a> that are remotely controlled from <a href="/wiki/Signalling_control" title="Signalling control">signalling control</a> centres in Munich and Leipzig.<sup id="cite_ref-deine-bahn-2015-6-12_132-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-deine-bahn-2015-6-12-132">[132]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-2016-01-10_133-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2016-01-10-133">[133]</a></sup> In 2014, the Federal Audit Office criticised the fact that the provision of €54 million for the signaling technology of the line had been made on the basis of an outdated operating program from 1995.<sup id="cite_ref-br-2014-241_50-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-br-2014-241-50">[50]</a></sup></p>
<p>For approximately 53&#160;km kilometers the line run in the open, usually on embankments (in the Main valley) or in cuttings.<sup id="cite_ref-pbde-1996_12-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pbde-1996-12">[12]</a></sup> The height of the embankments is limited to 15&#160;metres and the depth of the cuttings is limited to 20&#160;metres (under DB Directive&#160;836). Bridges and tunnels are built where these limits cannot be met. According to the introduction of 1997 EBA Directive <i>Anforderungen des Katastrophenschutzes an den Bau und den Betrieb von Eisenbahntunneln</i> ("requirements of disaster relief for the construction and operation of railway tunnels),<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup> railway tunnels that are at least 1000&#160;metres long am are used in mixed operation of passenger trains and freight trains must be operated as two separate single-track tubes. In coordination with the Federal Government, the states, the EBA and Deutsche Bahn, a concept was developed for the high-speed line with two tracks running through single tunnels, which allows a mixed train operation to be carried out on the line. The ETCS train safety system that has been used since 1997<sup id="cite_ref-br-2014-241_50-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-br-2014-241-50">[50]</a></sup> prohibits the operation of passenger and freight trains together as a <a href="/wiki/Fail-safe" title="Fail-safe">fail-safe</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-etr-2007-494_8-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-etr-2007-494-8">[8]</a></sup> According to the Federal Audit Office in 2014, it is not clear how this ban on trains meeting in tunnels should be implemented.<sup id="cite_ref-br-2014-241_50-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-br-2014-241-50">[50]</a></sup> Where necessary, measures mitigating <a href="/wiki/Piston_effect#Tunnel_Boom" title="Piston effect">tunnel boom</a> are also built in the portal area.<sup id="cite_ref-etr-2007-494_8-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-etr-2007-494-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<p>Two new <a href="/wiki/Traction_power_network" title="Traction power network">traction power lines</a> are used to supply power to the line (110&#160;kV). The 23.3&#160;kilometre-long southern line is to branch off at Wörlsdorf from the existing Nuremberg–<a href="/wiki/Weimar" title="Weimar">Weimar</a> line and end at the new Roth substation at the north portal of the Müß tunnel near Welchendorf in Thuringia.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup> The 21&#160;kilometre-long northern line leads from the new Eischleben substation to the Wolfsberg substation.<sup id="cite_ref-pbde-1996_12-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pbde-1996-12">[12]</a></sup> Over a length of about 4.4&#160;kilometres, the railway power line is carried through the Wipfra valley on 13 masts of a 380 kV transmission line, which runs from the Vieselbach substation to the <a href="/wiki/Altenfeld" title="Altenfeld">Altenfeld</a> substation. This eliminated the need for 15&#160;railway power line masts.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup> For energy supply and data transmission, moreover, there are approximately 1,200&#160;km of cable.<sup id="cite_ref-2016-01-10_133-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2016-01-10-133">[133]</a></sup></p>
<p>The 22 tunnels (ca. 40&#160;km) are equipped with, among other things, safety lighting, electrical equipment (power supply boxes) and test equipment for the overhead line voltage.<sup id="cite_ref-2016-01-10_133-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2016-01-10-133">[133]</a></sup> The line's technical equipment was commissioned in December 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-2016-01-10_133-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2016-01-10-133">[133]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Safety">Safety</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nuremberg%E2%80%93Erfurt_high-speed_railway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Safety">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In an "event in the tunnel", about 700 rescue workers from all districts along the route (of which far more than half are volunteers) are to be alerted, regardless of the exact incident. The only professional fire brigade is in Erfurt. The accesses to emergency exits are to be cleared of snow in winter.<sup id="cite_ref-ta-2015-05-19_137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ta-2015-05-19-137">[137]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span id="Nuremberg–Ebensfeld_upgraded_line"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Nuremberg.E2.80.93Ebensfeld_upgraded_line">Nuremberg–Ebensfeld upgraded line</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nuremberg%E2%80%93Erfurt_high-speed_railway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Nuremberg–Ebensfeld upgraded line">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<div style="display:inline;font-size:90%;"></div>
</td>
<td style="width:auto;padding:0;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center">

</td>
<td style="width:auto;padding:0;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center">
<table cellspacing="0" cellpadding="0" style="display: table; width: unset; line-height: 0; padding:0 !important; margin: 0 auto !important">
<tr style="display:inline-table;">
<td style="padding:0"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/BSicon_exSTR.svg/20px-BSicon_exSTR.svg.png" title="exSTR" width="20" height="20" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/BSicon_exSTR.svg/30px-BSicon_exSTR.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/BSicon_exSTR.svg/40px-BSicon_exSTR.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="500" /></td>

<td colspan="2" style="width:auto;vertical-align:middle;padding:0;text-align:left;">
<div style="display:inline;font-size:90%;">High-speed line</div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td style="width:auto;padding:0 3px 0 0;"></td>
<td style="width:auto;padding: 0;"></td>
<td style="width:auto;padding:0 3px;"></td>
<td style="width:auto;padding:0"></td>
<td style="width:auto;padding:0 3px;"></td>
<td style="width:auto;padding:0;"></td>
<td style="width:auto;padding:0 0 0 3px;"></td>
</tr>
</table>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td style="line-height:normal;text-align:right;padding:6px 5px 5px;">Source: German railway atlas<sup id="cite_ref-Eisenbahnatlas_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eisenbahnatlas-1">[1]</a></sup></td>
</tr>
</table>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>The 83&#160;km long line is part of the existing railway highway circuit from Nuremberg via <a href="/wiki/Saalfeld" title="Saalfeld">Saalfeld</a> to <a href="/wiki/Halle,_Saxony-Anhalt" class="mw-redirect" title="Halle, Saxony-Anhalt">Halle</a> and is being upgraded to a maximum speed up to 230&#160; km/h trains.</p>
<p>Between Nuremberg and Erlangen it is upgraded for up to 160&#160;km/h, between Erlangen and Ebensfeld for up to 230&#160;km/h.<sup id="cite_ref-etr-2010-558_138-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-etr-2010-558-138">[138]</a></sup> For about 41&#160;kilometres, the route will be operable at 230&#160;km/h, for about ten kilometres at 200&#160;km/h and otherwise at 160&#160;km/h.<sup id="cite_ref-eri-2015-514_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eri-2015-514-139">[139]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Situation_prior_to_the_upgrade">Situation prior to the upgrade</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nuremberg%E2%80%93Erfurt_high-speed_railway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Situation prior to the upgrade">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ebensfeld-Bahnhof-01.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Ebensfeld-Bahnhof-01.jpg/220px-Ebensfeld-Bahnhof-01.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Ebensfeld-Bahnhof-01.jpg/330px-Ebensfeld-Bahnhof-01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Ebensfeld-Bahnhof-01.jpg/440px-Ebensfeld-Bahnhof-01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5616" data-file-height="3744" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ebensfeld-Bahnhof-01.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The building, which was commissioned in 1846 and demolished in 2015, was a listed building in Ebensfeld</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In the section of line between Fürth and Bamberg, an <a href="/wiki/Intercity-Express" title="Intercity-Express">Intercity-Express</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Regional-Express" title="Regional-Express">Regional-Express</a> and an <a href="/wiki/S-Bahn" class="mw-redirect" title="S-Bahn">S-Bahn</a> run regularly (hourly in both directions).There are additional RE services every hour during the peak hours, resulting in a service every half hour. There is also an S-Bahn service to Forchheim every hour, so that all stops are served at least half-hourly between Nuremberg and Forchheim.</p>
<p>In the section between Bamberg and Ebensfeld an ICE, an RE (running as the Franken-Thüringen-Express) and a <a href="/wiki/Regionalbahn" title="Regionalbahn">Regionalbahn</a> (RB) service run hourly in both directions. The RE runs to <a href="/wiki/Hof_Hauptbahnhof" title="Hof Hauptbahnhof">Hof</a>/<a href="/wiki/Bayreuth_Hauptbahnhof" title="Bayreuth Hauptbahnhof">Bayreuth</a> on a two-hourly schedule, as do additional RE services on working days. Between Bamberg and Breitengussbach, <a href="/wiki/Agilis" title="Agilis">agilis</a> services run on the line every hour. In addition, about 60–70&#160;freight trains run each day.</p>
<p>Operational restrictions particularly affect in the Fürth district. Trains to Würzburg cross the tracks of trains from Bamberg, trains to and from the Nuremberg marshalling yard cross the tracks of the trains from Nuremberg Hbf to Würzburg (and vice versa). Since the completion of the extension of four tracks on the Nuremberg-Fürth section, the situation in Fürth has eased somewhat.</p>
<p>At Breitengüßbach and Zapfendorf stations between Bamberg and Ebensfeld, the access to the platforms was over a passenger level crossing, which meant that when regional services stopped, the track next to the station building had to be blocked for the safety of passengers.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Planning_2">Planning</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nuremberg%E2%80%93Erfurt_high-speed_railway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Planning">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The project was included in the Federal Transport Plan (<i>Bundesverkehrswegeplan</i>) 1992.</p>
<p>Between Nuremberg and Ebensfeld, different route options were tested:<sup id="cite_ref-etr-2007-494_8-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-etr-2007-494-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li>four-track upgrade of the Nuremberg–Fürth–Bamberg–Lichtenfels line</li>
<li>construction of a two-track line between Nuremberg and Großgründlach and upgrade the line between Großgründlach and Lichtenfels to four tracks</li>
<li>a two-track line on the left (western) side of the <a href="/wiki/Regnitz" title="Regnitz">Regnitz</a> to Bamberg followed by an additional two tracks between Bamberg and Lichtenfels</li>
<li>a new two-track line through <a href="/wiki/Franconian_Switzerland" title="Franconian Switzerland">Franconian Switzerland</a> from the Erlangen area to Hochstadt-Marktzeuln</li>
</ul>
<p>On 30 March 1993, the Bavarian State Ministry for Land Development and Environmental Issues initiated the land-use planning process.<sup id="cite_ref-pbde-1993-06_140-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pbde-1993-06-140">[140]</a></sup> In mid-1993<sup id="cite_ref-bmv-1995-8_22-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bmv-1995-8-22">[22]</a></sup> the spatial planning procedure was completed and the upgrade of the line to four tracks between Nuremberg and Ebensfeld was identified as the most favourable solution.<sup id="cite_ref-db-projektbau-2007-08_141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-db-projektbau-2007-08-141">[141]</a></sup> The first planning approval procedures were initiated in 1993.<sup id="cite_ref-etr-2007-494_8-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-etr-2007-494-8">[8]</a></sup> According to the planning status of mid-1993, the planning approval documents were expected to be available by October 1993 and the procedures were expected to continue until summer 1994. Construction approval was expected by autumn 1994 at the latest and the construction would then take five to six years.<sup id="cite_ref-pbde-1993-06_140-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pbde-1993-06-140">[140]</a></sup> According to another source, all 13 planning approval procedures of the upgrade were initiated in 1996; four were resolved by April 1997.<sup id="cite_ref-bmv-1997-04-19_64-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bmv-1997-04-19-64">[64]</a></sup></p>
<p>The line between Nuremberg and Fürth will receive an additional two tracks, with a pair of tracks being assigned to the <a href="/wiki/Nuremberg_S-Bahn" title="Nuremberg S-Bahn">Nuremberg S-Bahn</a> in the future. The 7.6&#160;kilometre-long line will be able to be operated at up to 160&#160;km/h.<sup id="cite_ref-db-projektbau-2007-08_141-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-db-projektbau-2007-08-141">[141]</a></sup> It will be possible to operate all four tracks in both directions and they will run directly to Nuremberg station. In addition to the four-track upgrade between Nuremberg and Fürth, there are several essentially local measures, in particular the elimination of <a href="/wiki/Level_crossing" title="Level crossing">level crossings</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-bt-16-1379_55-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bt-16-1379-55">[55]</a></sup></p>
<p>At Nuremberg station, platforms have to be adapted for the S-Bahn. Between the Nuremberg marshalling yard and Eltersdorf, the construction of a 13&#160;kilometre-long double-track freight line, including the 7,580&#160;metre-long <i>Pegnitz Tunnel</i> between Fürth-Kronach and Nuremberg-Grossmarkt is proposed. This would mean that the level junction at Fürth Hauptbahnhof could be abolished.<sup id="cite_ref-db-projektbau-2007-08_141-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-db-projektbau-2007-08-141">[141]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bt-16-5833_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bt-16-5833-142">[142]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-db-projektbau-2007-07-09_143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-db-projektbau-2007-07-09-143">[143]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-vde8-Flyer-pdf_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vde8-Flyer-pdf-144">[144]</a></sup></p>
<p>North of Fürth, the S-Bahn to Eltersdorf branches off the existing line. There, the existing line, the S-Bahn and the new line to Nuremberg freight yard will meet at a grade-separated junction.<sup id="cite_ref-etr-2007-494_8-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-etr-2007-494-8">[8]</a></sup> Between Fürth Hbf and Eltersdorf, the line will therefore have two tracks, with a third track in Vach station. From Eltersdorf, the existing line towards Erlangen/Bamberg will be supplemented to its east with two more tracks that can be operated at up to 230&#160;km/h.<sup id="cite_ref-db-projektbau-2007-08_141-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-db-projektbau-2007-08-141">[141]</a></sup> The line between Großgründlach and Bamberg will also be upgraded to four-tracks. The Nuremberg S-Bahn and freight traffic would use the two middle tracks.<sup id="cite_ref-bt-16-5833_142-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bt-16-5833-142">[142]</a></sup> The planned two tunnels of the extension would have a total length of eight kilometres and there would also be two new viaducts with a total length of 400&#160;metres.</p>
<p>The line on the section between Nuremberg and Bamberg meets the requirements of high-speed traffic as it is largely straight.<sup id="cite_ref-db-projektbau-2007-08_141-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-db-projektbau-2007-08-141">[141]</a></sup> It runs in the Regnitz valley almost in a straight line, particularly between Erlangen and Bamberg, and with curves with very large radii and can already be run largely at 160&#160;km/h. Between Fürth and Erlangen, there are some sharper curves, mainly between Fürth and Fürth-Unterfarrnbach,and north of Vach station (the underpass of the A&#160;73), and the speed is limited to 140&#160;km/h.</p>
<p>The extension is divided into thirteen sections for planning purposes and the planning approvals processes were initiated between 1994 and 1996. At the beginning of 1996, two decisions were made.<sup id="cite_ref-bmv-1996-04-14_24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bmv-1996-04-14-24">[24]</a></sup> From the beginning of July 1999<sup id="cite_ref-ek-2008-11-40_5-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ek-2008-11-40-5">[5]</a></sup> until 2002, the planning was based on the order of the Federal Ministry of Transport. As a result of changes in the technical and legal framework, planning amendments were initiated as of March 2002. In December 2001, the Free State of Bavaria let a contract for the planning of the proposed S-Bahn.<sup id="cite_ref-db-projektbau-2007-08_141-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-db-projektbau-2007-08-141">[141]</a></sup></p>
<p>The state of the planning for the southern planning assessment sections (<i>Planfeststellungsabschnitten</i>, PFA) is as follows:</p>
<ul>
<li>PFA 13 ("Nuremberg marshalling yard–Eltersdorf freight railway"): approval of the planning costs was put before the board of Deutsche Bahn AG for approval.<sup id="cite_ref-bt-16-5833_142-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bt-16-5833-142">[142]</a></sup> The planning of the freight railway, including the approximately 7,580&#160;metre-long Pegnitz Tunnel, was advertised Europe-wide on 21&#160;August 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-ted-2009.2FS_160-233174_145-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ted-2009.2FS_160-233174-145">[145]</a></sup></li>
<li>PFA 14 (the upgrade of the Nuremberg–Fürth line to four tracks): the section was planned and was opened in December 2010 (northern pair of tracks, line 5972 for the S-Bahn) and December 2011 (southern pair of tracks, line 5907). The newly built tracks are located on the (old) line 5900.</li>
<li>PFA 15 ("Fürth curve"): The planning approval decision was issued in August 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-bt-17-395_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bt-17-395-146">[146]</a></sup> The section was under construction from 2009 onwards. Completion was expected for 2013. However, due to a lack of connection to the rest of the network (PFA 16), it has not been possible to put it into operation.</li>
<li>PFA 16 ("Fürth North", relocation of the S-Bahn): the plan was established in February 2014, but it has not been finalised. The originally planned commissioning at the end of 2011 could not be achieved due to the lack of planning approval. The city of Fürth had threatened a complaint against the plan. It refused to approval the relocation of the S-Bahn and demanded that the S-Bahn be bundled with the existing line.</li>
<li>PFA 17 ("Erlangen"): The planning approval decision was issued in November 2009; the construction started in November 2011.</li>
<li>PFA 18/19 (Forchheim/Eggolsheim): the planning approval process had been discontinued in 1996 and 1997, but the planning approval process resumed 2013. Planning approval for the 14&#160;km-long section was given in January 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-vde8-pfa18_147-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vde8-pfa18-147">[147]</a></sup></li>
<li>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:ABS-Breiteng%C3%BC%C3%9Fbach-41.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/ABS-Breiteng%C3%BC%C3%9Fbach-41.jpg/220px-ABS-Breiteng%C3%BC%C3%9Fbach-41.jpg" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/ABS-Breiteng%C3%BC%C3%9Fbach-41.jpg/330px-ABS-Breiteng%C3%BC%C3%9Fbach-41.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/ABS-Breiteng%C3%BC%C3%9Fbach-41.jpg/440px-ABS-Breiteng%C3%BC%C3%9Fbach-41.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5616" data-file-height="3159" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:ABS-Breiteng%C3%BC%C3%9Fbach-41.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Separation of the new line south of Breitengüßbach</div>
</div>
</div>
The planning approval procedure was presented in April 1996 and the report of the hearing was presented in November 1996 and the procedure was suspended for the planning phase section 23/24, from the northern town limits of Bamberg to the northern edge of Marktes Zapfendorf. It was continued between 2013 and 2015 with three changes in planning procedures and concluded by an approval on 30 July 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-eba-2015-07-30_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eba-2015-07-30-148">[148]</a></sup> Construction work in section between Breitengüßbach (km&#160;68.9+73) and Zapfendorf (km&#160;77.7+07) began in 2015 and is due to be completed in late 2017 (status: February&#160;2014).<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup> The corresponding building contract was awarded to Leonhardt Weiss &amp; Co. KG in October 2015 for €145 million.<sup id="cite_ref-ted-2015.2FS_241-438278_150-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ted-2015.2FS_241-438278-150">[150]</a></sup> The mainline was completely blockaded from 11 January to 4 September 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-db-welt-s.C3.BCdost-2016-1-17_151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-db-welt-s.C3.BCdost-2016-1-17-151">[151]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-np-2014-07-30_152-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-np-2014-07-30-152">[152]</a></sup> The cost of the substitute buses was about €3.5 million.<sup id="cite_ref-nn-2016-01-13_153-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nn-2016-01-13-153">[153]</a></sup> The planning approval process also applied to changes at Nuremberg Hauptbahnhof.</li>
</ul>
<p>A total of 220&#160;kilometres tracks with 250 <a href="/wiki/Railroad_switch" title="Railroad switch">sets of points</a> and 160 bridges are to be built or rebuilt. At 26 railway stations, platforms are to be replaced or adapted, 25&#160;level crossings are to be closed and largely replaced by new overpasses and/or underpasses. Eleven level crossings had been eliminated by June 2007, and the planning or planning approval procedure had been initiated for nine level crossings.<sup id="cite_ref-db-projektbau-2007-08_141-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-db-projektbau-2007-08-141">[141]</a></sup></p>
<p>The environmental measures on the upgraded line include measures to increase biodiversity in the Fürther Rednitzgrund (between Stadeln and Vach) and the provision of financial resources to the city of Erlangen for measures to develop water courses.<sup id="cite_ref-db-projektbau-2007-08_141-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-db-projektbau-2007-08-141">[141]</a></sup></p>
<p>At the beginning of 1997, an upgrade for services up to 200&#160;km/h was proposed. There would also be several overtaking loops.<sup id="cite_ref-bmv-1997-04-19_64-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bmv-1997-04-19-64">[64]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Construction_2">Construction</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nuremberg%E2%80%93Erfurt_high-speed_railway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Construction">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In advance of the main projects, four bridges and the railway power supply have been renewed since 1996 in the area of the upgrade. Between 1998 and 2006, two substations were established.<sup id="cite_ref-db-projektbau-2007-08_141-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-db-projektbau-2007-08-141">[141]</a></sup></p>
<p>Work began on the provision of four tracks between Nuremberg and Fürth in 2006. The third track was put into operation at the end of 2010 at the fourth track followed in November 2011.</p>
<p>The further development is to be carried out gradually in accordance with the plan and as finance becomes available.<sup id="cite_ref-db-projektbau-2007-07-09_143-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-db-projektbau-2007-07-09-143">[143]</a></sup> Total funds of €370&#160;million have been provided for the upgrade between Nuremberg and Forchheim. Of this, approximately €200&#160;million is provided for the S-Bahn.<sup id="cite_ref-bt-16-5833_142-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bt-16-5833-142">[142]</a></sup> The upgrade of the 14&#160;kilometre-long section between Forchheim and Eggolsheim, which was scheduled to be carried out between 2011 and 2015, is estimated to cost €190&#160;million.<sup id="cite_ref-ted-347440-2010_154-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ted-347440-2010-154">[154]</a></sup> The eight-kilometer section south of Forchheim (km 31.2 to 39.7) was allocated €115 million through a joint venture.<sup id="cite_ref-ted-2016-093-166376_155-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ted-2016-093-166376-155">[155]</a></sup></p>
<p>Construction work on the 16-kilometre-long section from south of Eltersdorf through Erlangen to Baiersdorf, began in November&#160;2011. The section is being built in four sections and involves the rebuilding of various railway tracks and engineering structures.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup></p>
<p>The quadruplication of the section from Baiersdorf to Forchheim is to take place from 2016 to 2018, the extension to Neuses until 2022. Altogether this section is 13.5&#160;kilometres-long. The new tracks will be built to the east of the existing tracks. This work will cost €300&#160;million.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup></p>
<p>The quadruplication to Ebensfeld was expected to be completed by 2017, according to the planning goals of 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-db-2008-02-01_158-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-db-2008-02-01-158">[158]</a></sup> The federal government now expects (as of 2011) to complete the upgrade project (including for freight traffic) before 2025, with the delay being caused by a lack of finance.<sup id="cite_ref-hdb-2012-11_159-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hdb-2012-11-159">[159]</a></sup></p>
<p>The cost of planning approval section 25, between Zapfendorf (km 77.7+07) and Eierberge Tunnel (km 87.2+69), was finally established as €58,883,020 (net).<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup> Among other things, an overhauling facility with two relief loops will be built in Unterleiterbach.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">[161]</a></sup> The work was due to be completed by the end of 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">[162]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Costs_and_financing">Costs and financing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nuremberg%E2%80%93Erfurt_high-speed_railway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Costs and financing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>According to the federal government, of the estimated total costs of €5.36&#160;billion, (<a href="/wiki/Capital_budgeting#Net_present_value" title="Capital budgeting">net present value</a> of planning, land acquisition and construction costs) €2.668&#160;billion had already been spent in June 2013. This would mean the expenditure of €2.692&#160;billion was still outstanding.<sup id="cite_ref-vde-2013_1_163-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vde-2013_1-163">[163]</a></sup> The estimated cost of the Ebensfeld-Erfurt high-speed line amounted to €2.9&#160;billion (as of 2011).<sup id="cite_ref-newstix-2011-11-29_95-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-newstix-2011-11-29-95">[95]</a></sup> At the end of 2013, the estimated costs were reduced to €5.281&#160;billion. Of that, €3.012&#160;billion had been spent up to the end of 2013 and €2.268&#160;billion remained to be spent.<sup id="cite_ref-vde-2014_164-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vde-2014-164">[164]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2010, the total estimated cost of the project (new construction and upgraded line) was €5,224&#160;billion (as of 2010).<sup id="cite_ref-bmvbs-vde-2010_165-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bmvbs-vde-2010-165">[165]</a></sup> According to data from Deutsche Bahn, around €540&#160;million had been spent on the VDE&#160;8.1 project in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-haedrich-2012-06-08_123-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-haedrich-2012-06-08-123">[123]</a></sup></p>
<p>Financing agreements for around €2.1&#160;billion were still outstanding at the beginning of 2011. These were to be finalised when planning for the affected sections was completed.<sup id="cite_ref-bt-17-4410_116-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bt-17-4410-116">[116]</a></sup> At the end of 2007, the projected cost was about €5.069&#160;billion.<sup id="cite_ref-bmvbs-vde-2008_166-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bmvbs-vde-2008-166">[166]</a></sup> At the end of 2008, the total estimated cost was €5,178&#160;billion.<sup id="cite_ref-bt-17-444_29-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bt-17-444-29">[29]</a></sup></p>
<p>The new and upgraded lines were evaluated with a <a href="/wiki/Standardisierte_Bewertung" title="Standardisierte Bewertung">benefit-cost ratio</a> of 1.8.<sup id="cite_ref-bt-16.2F13561_167-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bt-16.2F13561-167">[167]</a></sup> The project is economically viable, based on a recent traffic forecast for 2025.<sup id="cite_ref-bt-17-4410_116-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bt-17-4410-116">[116]</a></sup></p>
<p>When the project was temporarily suspended in mid-1999, DM 620 million had been invested in the line.<sup id="cite_ref-sz-1999-07-09_168-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sz-1999-07-09-168">[168]</a></sup> Up to 31&#160;December 2005, €705&#160;million had been invested in the project, including about €550&#160;million for the high-speed line. In the following years, the total expenditure incurred for the planning and construction of the new line increased to €747&#160;million to the end of 2006,<sup id="cite_ref-bmvbs-vde-2007_169-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bmvbs-vde-2007-169">[169]</a></sup> €833&#160;million to the end of 2007,<sup id="cite_ref-bmvbs-vde-2008_166-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bmvbs-vde-2008-166">[166]</a></sup> €959&#160;million to the end of 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-bt-17-444_29-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bt-17-444-29">[29]</a></sup> and €1,225&#160;&#160;million to the end of 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-bmvbs-vde-2010_165-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bmvbs-vde-2010-165">[165]</a></sup> Around €1.7&#160;billion had been spent by mid-2011.<sup id="cite_ref-bmvbs-2011-08-29_170-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bmvbs-2011-08-29-170">[170]</a></sup></p>
<p>On the basis of a decision of the mediation committee of the <a href="/wiki/Bundestag" title="Bundestag">Bundestag</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Bundesrat_of_Germany" title="Bundesrat of Germany">Bundesrat</a>, the provision of federal funds for the route were significantly reduced in December 2003.<sup id="cite_ref-bt-16-1379_55-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bt-16-1379-55">[55]</a></sup> According to the Federal Government's investment plan for the transport infrastructure, €741.4&#160;million was allocated to the project in the period 2006–2010. The funding requirement that is in excess of the €3.641&#160;billion of federal funds as of 2011 is to be provided by Deutsche Bahn's own funds and third parties.<sup id="cite_ref-bmvbs-2007-04_171-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bmvbs-2007-04-171">[171]</a></sup> The state of Thuringia is investing a total of €240&#160;million from the European Regional Fund in the two high-speed line projects (Nuremberg–Erfurt and Erfurt–Leipzig/Halle).<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">[172]</a></sup></p>
<p>In December 2008, the Federal Minister of Transport, Wolfgang Tiefensee announced that additional funds would be available so that it could be commissioned in 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-fw-2008-12-03_173-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fw-2008-12-03-173">[173]</a></sup> From 2010 onwards, more than €200&#160;million was to be made available by the federal government.<sup id="cite_ref-ParlUnterst.C3.BCtzer2008_112-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ParlUnterst.C3.BCtzer2008-112">[112]</a></sup> At the latest from 2013 onwards, the railway would receive an annual budgetary allocation of €350&#160;million.<sup id="cite_ref-freies-wort-2007-12-12_174-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-freies-wort-2007-12-12-174">[174]</a></sup></p>
<p>The planned total costs for the new line were €2.7&#160;billion in early 2010. Until then, construction contracts of €1.2&#160;billion had been awarded. For the sections under construction, tenders had still not been let for construction amounting to €340&#160;million. Between €149 and €214&#160;million are being provided each year between 2010 and 2017. Between €17 and €60&#160;billion were provided between 2010 and 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-bt-17-451_52-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bt-17-451-52">[52]</a></sup> The Federal Government is providing €2.2&#160;billion of the finance for the new line.<sup id="cite_ref-bmvbs-2011-08-29_170-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bmvbs-2011-08-29-170">[170]</a></sup></p>
<p>At the beginning of construction of the new line, on 16&#160;April 1996, the cost of the entire Nuremberg–Erfurt project were calculated to be about DM 8.5&#160;billion.<sup id="cite_ref-sz-1996-04-17-46_28-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sz-1996-04-17-46-28">[28]</a></sup> The financial agreement for the new line was signed on 10&#160;November 1997.<sup id="cite_ref-bt-17-444_29-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bt-17-444-29">[29]</a></sup> This also included individual measures for the upgraded line.<sup id="cite_ref-bt-16-1379_55-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bt-16-1379-55">[55]</a></sup> The construction timetable and financial plan laid down in the financing agreement could no longer be complied with due to reduced budgets as a result of a compromise negotiated in the mediation committee in December 2003.<sup id="cite_ref-bt-16-1379_55-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bt-16-1379-55">[55]</a></sup></p>
<p>In September 2005 an agreement was reached on the Nuremberg–Fürth section. The financing arrangements do not have any cost ceilings; the Federal Government bears the risk of cost increases.<sup id="cite_ref-bt-16-1379_55-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bt-16-1379-55">[55]</a></sup> The financial agreements for the section between Nuremberg and Fürth as well as between Ebensfeld and Erfurt are updated annually.<sup id="cite_ref-bundestag-16-11730_175-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bundestag-16-11730-175">[175]</a></sup> The planned share of Deutsche Bahn AG in the overall project is included in the €158.4&#160;million, that is €63.0&#160;million for the new line.<sup id="cite_ref-bt-16-1379_55-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bt-16-1379-55">[55]</a></sup></p>
<p>Individual financial agreements between the Federal Government and the business sectors of DB&#160;Netz, <a href="/wiki/DB_Station%26Service" title="DB Station&amp;Service">DB Station&amp;Service</a> and DB&#160;Energie covered the financing of the project as a whole. As part of the <a href="/wiki/Trans-European_Networks" title="Trans-European Networks">Trans-European Networks</a>, the project benefits from co-finance in part from the <a href="/wiki/European_Regional_Development_Fund" title="European Regional Development Fund">European Regional Development Fund</a> (ERDF). In the 2007-2013 funding period, ERDF funds from the "Operational Program Transport" in the amount of €239.3&#160;million were planned;<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">[176]</a></sup> these were approved on 20 November 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">[177]</a></sup></p>
<p>In mid-1993 the estimated costs of the approximately 196&#160;kilometre-long new and upgraded line was about DM 7.196&#160;billion.<sup id="cite_ref-bmv-1993-71_10-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bmv-1993-71-10">[10]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-pbde-1993-06_140-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pbde-1993-06-140">[140]</a></sup> In 1994, DB&#160;AG estimated the cost of the 109&#160;kilometre-long new line as DM 4.044&#160;billion (€2.068 billion; 1994 prices).<sup id="cite_ref-spiegel-1997-40-20_178-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-spiegel-1997-40-20-178">[178]</a></sup> At the start of construction, in April 1996, the costs were calculated as DM 8.3&#160; billion (about €4.2&#160;billion ).<sup id="cite_ref-ek-2008-11-40_5-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ek-2008-11-40-5">[5]</a></sup> The increase in costs was caused by the conversion of costs from real to (inflation-adjusted) nominal values<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">[179]</a></sup> and increased technical requirements.<sup id="cite_ref-freies-wort-2007-07-16_85-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-freies-wort-2007-07-16-85">[85]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bmvbs-vde-2010_165-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bmvbs-vde-2010-165">[165]</a></sup></p>
<p>In addition, funds from a stimulatory package in response to the <a href="/wiki/Financial_crisis_of_2007%E2%80%932008" title="Financial crisis of 2007–2008">financial crisis of 2007–2008</a> have been applied to the line.<sup id="cite_ref-bams-2009-01-18_180-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bams-2009-01-18-180">[180]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Criticism">Criticism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nuremberg%E2%80%93Erfurt_high-speed_railway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Criticism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:ICE-Protestpostkarte-1994_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/ICE-Protestpostkarte-1994_1.jpg/220px-ICE-Protestpostkarte-1994_1.jpg" width="220" height="158" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/ICE-Protestpostkarte-1994_1.jpg/330px-ICE-Protestpostkarte-1994_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/ICE-Protestpostkarte-1994_1.jpg/440px-ICE-Protestpostkarte-1994_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="358" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:ICE-Protestpostkarte-1994_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Postcard of the Citizen Initiative Das bessere Bahnkonzept (<i>The better railway concept</i>) against the new line (1994)</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Protestbanner_gegen_L%C3%A4rmschutzw%C3%A4nde_Bamberg.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Protestbanner_gegen_L%C3%A4rmschutzw%C3%A4nde_Bamberg.jpg/170px-Protestbanner_gegen_L%C3%A4rmschutzw%C3%A4nde_Bamberg.jpg" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Protestbanner_gegen_L%C3%A4rmschutzw%C3%A4nde_Bamberg.jpg/255px-Protestbanner_gegen_L%C3%A4rmschutzw%C3%A4nde_Bamberg.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Protestbanner_gegen_L%C3%A4rmschutzw%C3%A4nde_Bamberg.jpg/340px-Protestbanner_gegen_L%C3%A4rmschutzw%C3%A4nde_Bamberg.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1920" data-file-height="2560" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Protestbanner_gegen_L%C3%A4rmschutzw%C3%A4nde_Bamberg.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Protest banner in Bamberg against the planned noise barriers</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The construction of the route has been criticised for various reasons. Some criticism relates to the route, since it is not possible to bundle different ICE routes over the line. Therefore, as with the existing <a href="/wiki/Franconian_Forest_Railway" title="Franconian Forest Railway">Franconian Forest Railway</a>, only one long-distance train service per hour and each way can be expected.</p>
<p>Critics such as <a href="/wiki/Alliance_%2790/The_Greens" class="mw-redirect" title="Alliance '90/The Greens">Alliance '90/The Greens</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bund_f%C3%BCr_Umwelt_und_Naturschutz_Deutschland" title="Bund für Umwelt und Naturschutz Deutschland">Bund für Umwelt und Naturschutz Deutschland</a> believed the project is pointless and a waste of public funds. They proposed instead to upgrade the rail network in northern Bavaria.<sup id="cite_ref-sz-1996-04-17-46_28-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sz-1996-04-17-46-28">[28]</a></sup> <i>Vieregg-Rössler</i> (a consultancy), the Greens and the <i>Verkehrsclub Deutschland</i> (a lobby group for environmentally-friendly transport solutions, VCD) suggested at the end of 1992 that traffic should run from Erfurt via Gera, Plauen and Hof to Nuremberg.<sup id="cite_ref-sz-1992-11-21_181-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sz-1992-11-21-181">[181]</a></sup> Since 1992, <i>Das bessere Bahnkonzept</i> ("The better railway concept") has acted as the umbrella organisation for the citizen initiatives that oppose the line.</p>
<p>On the brink of a joint meeting of the Bavarian and Thuringian state cabinets, citizens' lists with around 50,000 signatures were submitted against the project and against the A&#160;73 autobahn project.<sup id="cite_ref-sz-1994-01-26_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sz-1994-01-26-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<p>Representatives of Deutsche Bahn also repeatedly criticised the project. Thus, in April 1997, the former DB Chairman, <a href="/wiki/Heinz_D%C3%BCrr" title="Heinz Dürr">Heinz Dürr</a> told the Transport Committee of the Deutsche Bundestag that the route "does not count particularly". The head of the urban transport division wrote in the same year that the route made "no entrepreneurial sense."<sup id="cite_ref-sz-1999-05-29_35-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sz-1999-05-29-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<p>Nature conservationists criticised the far-reaching impacts of the new line on the landscape and called it the "most expensive U-Bahn in the world".<sup id="cite_ref-sz-1999-05-29_35-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sz-1999-05-29-35">[35]</a></sup> The transport scientist Heiner Monheim demanded the end of construction in 2007. Instead of the large-scale project, numerous smaller measures would bring about improvements in the area. The majority of the customers did not need the route, just "the construction industry, so that they deserve a golden nose, or speed fetishists dreaming of a high-speed network in Europe."<sup id="cite_ref-otz-2007-10-28_182-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-otz-2007-10-28-182">[182]</a></sup></p>
<p>A citizens' initiative was launched around 2009 promoting a route via <a href="/wiki/Lichtenfels,_Bavaria" title="Lichtenfels, Bavaria">Lichtenfels</a>, along the <a href="/wiki/Bundesautobahn_73" title="Bundesautobahn 73">A&#160;73</a>, which according to its information would have been €0.5 billion cheaper than the route planned south of Coburg.<sup id="cite_ref-np-coburg-2007-09-08_183-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-np-coburg-2007-09-08-183">[183]</a></sup> The Federal Ministry of Transport rejected the proposed route due to its significant impacts.<sup id="cite_ref-np-coburg-2007-10-02_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-np-coburg-2007-10-02-3">[3]</a></sup> The Ministry also doubted the achievable savings on the basis of the proposed passage through Lichtenfels, Schney and <a href="/wiki/Grub_am_Forst" title="Grub am Forst">Grub am Forst</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-coburg-2008-08-16_184-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-coburg-2008-08-16-184">[184]</a></sup></p>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Bamberg" title="Bamberg">Bamberg</a> the upgrade plans caused protests among the citizens, as DB planned to build high noise barriers. Subsequently, the plans were rejected. Three new options emerged from a dialogue: optimised new noise protection on the existing route, which would be lowered at sensitive points, a tunnel for freight trains or a complete bypass of Bamberg to the east through the main stretch of <a href="/wiki/Carr_(landform)" title="Carr (landform)">carr</a> (marshy forest), parallel to the A&#160;73. The current draft of the Federal Transport Plan (<i>Bundesverkehrswegeplan</i>) for 2030 includes the bypass along the A 73 because it has the best benefit/cost ratio.</p>
<p>Prior to the application for planning approval on 2 May 2016, the Bamberg council passed a resolution by a majority on 27 April 2016 that rejected an eastern bypass. It is feared that the ICE stop at Bamberg station would be abandoned. The planning approval process is expected to commence by the spring of 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">[185]</a></sup></p>

<th scope="row" class="navbox-group" style="width:1%">China<br />
(Mainland)</th>
<td class="navbox-list navbox-odd" style="text-align:left;border-left-width:2px;border-left-style:solid;width:100%;padding:0px">
<div style="padding:0em 0.25em">(* Indicates overlap with conventional services)
